Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Identifying Isti'ara (Metaphor) in Commentarial Introductions
Commentator explains rhetorical praise of the Sultan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify types of isti'ara (explicit, implicit, and imaginative attribution) in a commentarial passage and explain their function.

Core Idea
Metaphor analysis is a key skill for reading logical texts without confusion.

The opening praise of the Sultan in this commentary is filled with figurative language. The commentators, al-Dasuqi and al-Attar, meticulously dissect each metaphor to clarify meaning. Understanding their method will help you approach similar rhetorical passages in other Islamic scholarly works, where metaphor often carries precise legal or theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the base phrase
Identify the original phrase from the matn (e.g., 'قامع آثار الظلم') that the commentator is explaining. Read the commentary to see which part is being analyzed.
The base text is typically the bold or quoted part.
2
Identify the claimed isti'ara type
Note whether the commentator explicitly names the type: tasrihiyya (explicit), makniyya (implicit), or takhyil (imaginative attribution). Record the term used.
For example, al-Dasuqi says 'ففيه استعارة' (there is isti'ara) and later specifies 'على طريق المكنية' (via implicit metaphor).
3
Determine what is likened to what
Analyze the simile or comparison: what is the tenor (the subject) and what is the vehicle (the image)? For instance, traces of injustice are likened to tyrannical men.
The commentator may explicitly state the comparison, e.g., 'شبه آثار الظلم برجال جائرين'.
4
Distinguish literal vs. figurative meaning
Check the commentator's explanation of the intended meaning. For example, 'قامع' literally means 'humiliator' but here means 'remover', indicating a metaphorical extension.
This step reveals how figurative language conveys the author's intended praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدْمَةُ الشارح
قامعُ آثارِ الظُلمِ والاعتِسافِ، مُحيِي مآثِرِ السُّنَّةِ النَّبويَّة، مُنَفِّذُ أحكام الملَّةِ المصطَفَويَّة، هو الَّذِي يُعِزُّ الدِّينَ
الدسوقي
: مُرادف ، والإنصافُ في الأصل إعطاء النّصفة، يُقالُ : فلان نصفَ أَخاهُ؛ أي: جعل الأمر بينهما نصفين، ولكنَّ المراد به هنا : أن يعطي كلَّ أحدٍ حقَّهُ على الوجه الشَّرعيّ، وهو عين العدل. (قَوْلُهُ : قَامِعُ ) أي : مُذِلُّ، والمراد به المزيل، ففيه استعارة لا تخفى عليك، أو أنَّه شبَّهَ آثارَ الظلم وهو الجورُ برجالٍ جائرين على طريقِ المكنية، وإثبات قامع تخييل . (قَوْلُهُ : وَالِاعْتِسَافِ) عطفٌ مُرادف ، والاعتسافُ في الأصل: اسم للمشي على غيرِ الطَّريقِ الحسّيّ، أُطلق هنا على الظلم، وهو المشي على غيرِ الطَّريقِ الشَّرعيّ، فهو مجاز، علاقته الإطلاق والتقييد. (قَوْلُهُ: مُحْيِي مَآثِرِ أي مكارم والسُّنَّة الطَّريقة، والمراد بالمآثر : الأحكام الشَّرعيَّة، فهي مُستعار لها ، ثمَّ شُبّهت تلك المآثر بمعنى الأحكام الشَّرعيَّةِ من حيثُ خفاؤها قبل وجود هذا الممدوح بموتى على طريق المكنية، وإثباتُ مُحيي تخييل؛ إما باق على حقيقتِه أو مُستعارٌ لمظهر . (قَوْلُهُ : مُنَفِّذُ أَحْكَامِ الْمِلَّةِ الإضافة للبيان، وقوله: (المصطفوية)؛ نسبةٌ للمصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلَّم، ومنفّذ؛ إما بالفاء وهو ظاهر، وإما بالقاف؛ أي: مُخلّص لها، وعليه فشبه الأحكام من حيثُ عدمُ العمل بها قبل وجود هذا الممدوح برجال استحوذ عليهم ظالم واضطرُّوا لِمَنْ يُنقذهم منهُ تشبيهاً مُضمراً في النَّفْسِ على طريق الاستعارة بالكناية، وإثباتُ الإنقاذ تخييل ؛ أي: أنَّه مُخلِّص لها من الضياع والتَّرْكِ بإظهارها والعمل بمقتضاها . (قَوْلُهُ: هُوَ) أي : السُّلطان . (قَوْلُهُ: يُعِزُّ) أي: يُقوّي الدِّيْنَ، وهو الأحكامُ الشَّرعيَّة، والمراد بتقويتها : إظهارها وتنفيذها والجري على مقتضاها ؛ بحيثُ لا يتعطَّل حكم منها .
العطار
بالسَّيفِ والسَّنَانِ، ويَنصُرُه بالحُجَّةِ والبرهان، تَلالات على صفحات الأيَّام آثارُ مَعْدِلَتِه وسلطانه، وتهللَتْ على وَجْنَاتِ الأنام أنوارُ مَكْرُمَته
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : بالسيف) أي : بالقتل به في الجهاد والسنان؛ أي: الرماح ؛ أي: فكان يُجاهد في سبيل الله . (قَوْلُهُ : وَيَنْصُرُهُ ... إلخ) أي : فكان يقوّي ذلك، فجمع ذلك الشلطان بين العلم والجهاد. (قَوْلُهُ : بِالْحُجَّةِ) أي : الدَّليل، وعطفُ البرهان من عطب الخاص على العام. (قَوْلُهُ : تَلَالَأَتْ) أي : أضاءَتْ وأشرقَتْ، وهو مُستعار لظهرت، استعارة تصريحية تبعية، وصفحات الأيَّام ؛ أي: جوانبُ أيَّامِهِ، فأل في الأَيَّامِ عوض عن المضاف إليه، فشبَّه أيَّامَهُ بقصور لها صفحات؛ أي جوانب على طريق المكنية، وصفحات : تخييل . (قَوْلُهُ : أَثَارُ مَعْدِلَتِهِ) أي : عدله والمراد بآثارِهِ: انتظام حالِ الرَّعيَّةِ، وسُلطانه؛ :أي: قهره ؛ أي: للكفَّار، ولا يخفى ما في الكلام من الاستعارة بالكناية؛ حيثُ شبَّهَ انتظامَ حالِ الرَّعيَّةِ الَّذي هو أثرُ العدلِ والسَّلطنة بنورٍ يُضيء، ويُشرقُ على طريقِ المكنية، وإثباتُ التَّلألؤ تخييل . (قَوْلُهُ : وَتَهَلَّلَتْ) عطف مرادف على تلألأت . (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى وَجَنَاتِ الْأَنَامِ جمعُ وجنة ؛ وهي ما ارتفع من الوجه، وقوله: أنوارُ مكرمته؛ أي: عدله، فقوله : وإحسانه عطفٌ مُغاير، أو أنَّ المراد بمكرميه كَرمُهُ، فالعطفُ تفسيريٌّ، ولا يخفى ما في الكلام من الاستعارة؛ حيثُ شبَّهَ
العطّار
(قَوْلُهُ : تَلَأُلَأَتْ) أي: أشرقت ، والصَّفحاتُ جَمعُ صفحة؛ وهي مِنَ الوجه والسَّيف عرضه، وإضافتها للأيَّامِ كَلْجَينِ الماء، والمعدلة: العدل، والوجنات : يفتح الواو وقد تُثَلَّثُ؛ مَا ارتفعَ مِن لَحَمةِ خَدٌ الإنسان، والتذهيبُ: الطَّلاءُ بالذَّهَبِ، فَفِيهِ مَدح لشرحه، والميامِنُ : جمعُ يُمن ؛ بمعنى البركة، والملامح : جَمْعُ ملمح ؛ بمعنى اللمح، والرِّداءُ : ما يُرتدى بِهِ ، وَرِدَاءُ العزّ كَلُجَينِ الماء.
Introduction of the Commentator: The suppressor of the traces of injustice and oppression, reviver of the effects of the Prophetic Sunnah, executor of the rulings of the Chosen creed, He who strengthens the religion. al-Dasuqi: It is synonymous; equity (insaf) originally means giving half; it is said: So-and-so treated his brother equitably, i.e., he made the matter between them halves, but what is meant here is that he gives everyone his right in a lawful manner, and that is precisely justice. (His saying: 'Suppressor') i.e., humiliator; what is meant is the remover; thus there is in it an isti'ara (metaphor) that is not hidden from you, or that he likened the traces of injustice, which is tyranny, to tyrannical men via the way of mikniya (implicit metaphor), and establishing 'suppressor' is takhyil (imaginative attribution). (His saying: 'and oppression') is a synonymous conjunction; oppression originally means walking on a non-sensory path; it is used here for injustice, which is walking on a non-legal path; so it is a metaphor, its relationship is absoluteness and restriction. (His saying: 'reviver of effects') i.e., generosities; and 'Sunnah' means the path; what is meant by 'effects' are the legal rulings; thus it is metaphorically used for them; then those effects, meaning the legal rulings, were likened, in terms of their obscurity before the existence of this praised one, to the dead via the way of mikniya, and establishing 'reviver' is takhyil; either remaining in its literal sense or metaphorically used for a manifestation. (His saying: 'executor of the rulings of the creed') the annexation is for clarification; and his saying: 'the Chosen' is a relative attribution to the Chosen One, may God bless him and grant him peace; and 'executor' is either with 'fa' which is apparent, or with 'qaf' meaning 'deliverer'; accordingly, he likened the rulings, in terms of the lack of acting upon them before the existence of this praised one, to men captured by a tyrant and forced to seek someone to rescue them, as an implicit simile in the mind via the way of isti'ara bil-kinnaya (allusive metaphor), and establishing 'rescue' is takhyil; i.e., he delivers them from loss and abandonment by manifesting them and acting according to them. (His saying: 'He') i.e., the Sultan. (His saying: 'strengthens') i.e., strengthens the religion, which is the legal rulings; what is meant by strengthening them is manifesting them, executing them, and proceeding according to them such that no ruling is suspended. al-Attar: With the sword and the spear, and supports it with proof and demonstration; the traces of his justice and authority glittered on the pages of days; and the lights of his generosity brightened on the cheeks of people. al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'with the sword') i.e., by killing with it in jihad; 'spear' i.e., lances; i.e., he would strive in the path of God. (His saying: 'and supports it... etc.') i.e., he would strengthen that; so that sultan combined knowledge and jihad. (His saying: 'with proof') i.e., evidence; the coordination of 'demonstration' is from coordinating the specific to the general. (His saying: 'glittered') i.e., shone and radiated; it is metaphorically used for 'appeared', an explicit derivative metaphor; 'pages of days' i.e., the aspects of his days; the 'al' in 'al-ayyam' substitutes for the annexed term; thus he likened his days to palaces having pages, i.e., sides, via the way of mikniya; 'pages' is takhyil. (His saying: 'traces of his justice') i.e., his justice; what is meant by 'its traces' is the orderly condition of the subjects; 'his authority' i.e., his dominance over the disbelievers; and what is in the speech of isti'ara bil-kinnaya is not hidden; where he likened the orderly condition of the subjects, which is the effect of justice and sovereignty, to a light that illuminates and shines via the way of mikniya; and establishing 'glittering' is takhyil. (His saying: 'and brightened') is a synonymous conjunction to 'glittered'. (His saying: 'on the cheeks of people' plural of 'wajna', which is the raised part of the face; and his saying: 'lights of his generosity' i.e., his justice; so his saying 'and his beneficence' is a different conjunction, or what is meant by his generosity is his magnanimity; thus the conjunction is explanatory; what is in the speech of isti'ara is not hidden; where he likened... al-Attar: (His saying: 'glittered') i.e., shone; 'pages' plural of 'safha', which from the face and the sword is its width; its annexation to 'days' is like the jugs of water; 'al-mu'dila' is justice; 'wajanat' with open waw and possibly triple vowels; the raised flesh of a human cheek; 'al-tadhheeb' is plating with gold, thus it contains praise for his commentary; 'al-mayamin' plural of 'yumn' meaning blessing; 'al-malamih' plural of 'milmah' meaning glance; 'al-rida' is what is worn; and the garment of honor is like the jugs of water.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary (sharh) on an introductory logic text, likely al-Tadhheeb or similar. The commentator begins by praising the ruler, using elaborate rhetorical figures common in classical Islamic panegyrics. The passage consists of two main layers: the original text (likely a poetic or rhythmic praise) and the explanatory gloss by the commentators al-Dasuqi and al-Attar. The commentary explains each phrase in turn, focusing on the metaphorical language (isti'ara) and its subtypes: explicit (tasrihiyya), implicit (makniyya), and imaginative attribution (takhyeel). For example, the phrase 'suppressor of traces of injustice and oppression' is explained as a metaphor likening injustice to tyrants, and 'suppressor' is imaginative attribution. The phrase 'reviver of effects of the Sunnah' is analyzed: 'effects' are legal rulings, which were obscure before the ruler revived them, likened to the dead. Similarly, 'executor of rulings' involves a parallel metaphor of rescuing captured men. The second part continues with praise of the ruler's combination of military strength (sword, spear) and intellectual proof (hujja, burhan), symbolizing jihad and knowledge. The enduring legacy of his justice is described as glittering on the pages of days, likening days to palaces with visible sides. The commentators carefully dissect each figurative expression, illustrating their expertise in Arabic rhetoric. This section is front matter, establishing the commentator's respect for the patron, but it also demonstrates the analytical method that will be applied to logical concepts later.

Key Terms
الِاسْتِعَارَة (al-isti'ara): metaphorical transfer
الْمِكْنِيَّة (al-mikniyya): implicit metaphor
التَّخْيِيل (al-takhyeel): imaginative attribution
الْعَدْل (al-'adl): justice

Checkpoint

B) Implicit (makniyya) with takhyil
C) Imaginative attribution only

Key Takeaway
The commentator's rhetorical analysis demonstrates that figurative language is pervasive even in logical texts, and understanding it is a prerequisite for precise logical reasoning.

Defining al-Muta‘ and al-Muti‘ lil-Shar‘
Commentator defines the terms 'al-muta‘' and 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘' with two interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of 'al-shar‘' in the definition of 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘' and explain how each affects the meaning.

Core Idea
The same phrase can carry two distinct meanings depending on how we interpret 'al-shar‘'.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies two key attributes of the Sultan: that he is obeyed (al-muta‘) and that he is obedient to the Shari‘ah (al-muti‘ lil-shar‘). The second term is particularly nuanced because the word 'shar‘' can refer either to the legal rulings or to the Lawgiver Himself. Understanding this ambiguity is essential for precise reasoning about authority and obedience in Islamic governance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms being defined
Find 'al-muta‘' and 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘' in the Arabic. Note that the commentator gives separate definitions for each.
2
Extract the definition of 'al-muta‘'
The commentator says: 'al-muta‘' means the one whom people obey, so they act according to his word. Write down the genus (the one whom people obey) and differentia (they act according to his word).
3
Analyze the two interpretations of 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘'
The commentator splits the definition based on the meaning of 'shar‘'. First, if 'shar‘' means the Shari‘ah rulings, then obedience means acting according to those rulings. Second, if 'shar‘' means the Lawgiver (Allah), then obedience means compliance with His commands and prohibitions.
This is the core expansion of the passage.
4
Compare the two interpretations
How does the object of obedience change? In the first, it is a set of rules; in the second, it is a Person. What implications does each have for the Sultan's role?
This highlights the importance of disambiguating terms in definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : الْمُطَاعُ) أي : الذي تُطيعُهُ الأنام، فيعملون بمقتضى قوله، وقوله: المطيع لِلشَّرع؛ إنْ أُريدَ بِهِ الأحكامُ الشَّرعيَّة ؛ فالمراد بإطاعته له العمل بمقتضاه، وإنْ كانَ المراد بالشَّرعِ الشّارع؛ فالمراد بإطاعته له الامتثال لأوامره ونواهيه بالفعل والتَّوْكِ .
His statement: 'al-muta‘' means the one whom people obey, so they act according to his word. And his statement: 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘' if by 'shar‘' is meant the legal rulings, then the meaning of his obedience to it is acting according to it. And if by 'shar‘' is meant the Lawgiver, then the meaning of his obedience to Him is compliance with His commands and prohibitions in action and reliance.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defining two attributes of the Sultan in the original text: 'al-muta‘' (the obeyed) and 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘' (the obedient to the Shari‘ah). The commentator explains 'al-muta‘' as the one whom the people obey, meaning they act in accordance with his command. This is a straightforward definition. Then he turns to 'al-muti‘ lil-shar‘', noting that the word 'shar‘' can be interpreted in two ways: either it refers to the Shari‘ah rulings (ahkam shar‘iyya) or to the Lawgiver (al-shari‘) himself. If it is the former, then the Sultan's obedience means he acts in accordance with those rulings. If it is the latter, then his obedience means he complies with God's commands and prohibitions in his actions and relies upon Him. This dual interpretation shows the commentator's linguistic awareness and ensures the phrase is understood comprehensively. There is no logical argument here; it is purely definitional commentary.

Key Terms
المطاع
المطيع للشرع
الشرع

Precise definition requires disambiguating key terms like 'shar‘' to avoid equivocation.

Unpacking the Supplication for the Sultan's Eternal Rule
Commentator explains the prayer phrases for the Sultan's lasting authority, power, and honor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the key terms (mulk, sultan, sha'n, a'wan, jaysh) in the supplication for the Sultan's eternal rule, as interpreted by the commentator.

Core Idea
Every word in a prayer carries precise meaning; the commentator unpacks each term to reveal its theological and political weight.

The commentator’s explanation of this supplication shows how classical scholars carefully defined even the most familiar terms in prayers for the ruler. By examining the commentary, we learn how each word contributes to a comprehensive benediction for the Sultan’s authority, power, and honor. This lesson will guide you through the key phrases and their lexical nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main supplication phrase
Locate the central prayer 'khallid allahumma mulkahu' in the Arabic and note that the commentator introduces it as the supplication with which he adorned his commentary.
The phrase is a request for the Sultan's kingdom to be made eternal.
2
Parse the meaning of 'mulk' and 'khallid'
Find the commentator's definition: 'mulk' is authority over subjects by command and prohibition; 'khallid' means eternal, without end.
'Khallid' is a verb in the form of a supplication.
3
Examine 'sultanahu' and 'wa a'li'
Sultan is defined as domination over enemies; 'wa a'li' means execute his word and elevate his stature (sha'n) and helpers (a'wan).
The term 'sultan' here refers to power, not the title.
4
Analyze grammatical relations
Understand the syntactic connections: 'jayshahu' (his army) is related to 'khallid' or is a circumstantial qualifier; 'da'imah' and 'qaimah' both mean continuous/perpetual.
This shows the commentator's attention to grammatical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : خَلّدِ اللَّهُمَّ مُلْكَهُ هذا هو الدُّعاءُ الَّذي وشَحَ بِهِ شَرحَهُ ؛ أي: اللَّهُمَّ اجعلْ مُلْكَهُ ؛ أي : تصرُّفَهُ في الرَّعيَّةِ بالأمر والنهي مُخلَّداً ؛ أي: دائماً لا انقضاء له. (قَوْلُهُ: وَسُلْطَانَهُ) أي : قهره للأعداء . (قَوْلُهُ : وَأَعْل) أي : نفّذ كلمته وشأنَه ؛ أي: قدْرَهُ ومرتبته وأعوانه ؛ أي : مُعينيه ؛ كانت طائفته أم لا . (قَوْلُهُ : جَيْشَهُ) أي : طوائفَه في دولة ؛ أي: جماعة أو سلطنة، متعلّق بخلد، أو حال من ضمير ملكه . (قَوْلُهُ : : دَائِمَةٍ) أي : مُستمرّة، وقوله: قائمة؛ أي: دائمة.
His statement: 'O Allah, perpetuate his kingdom' — this is the supplication with which he adorned his commentary. That is: O Allah, make his kingdom — i.e., his authority over the subjects by command and prohibition — eternal, i.e., perpetual with no end. (His statement: 'and his sultan' means his domination over enemies. (His statement: 'and raise' means execute his word and his stature, i.e., his rank and position, and his helpers, i.e., his supporters, whether they be his group or not. (His statement: 'his army' means his troops in a state, i.e., a group or sultanate, related to 'perpetuate' or a circumstantial qualifier from the pronoun of his kingdom. (His statement: 'everlasting' means continuous, and his statement: 'enduring' means perpetual.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the supplication included in the original text. The commentator explains each phrase of the prayer for the Sultan. He begins with 'khallid allahumma mulkahu' (O Allah, perpetuate his kingdom), noting that this prayer is a decoration (washah) of the commentary. 'Mulk' is interpreted as the Sultan's authority over subjects through command and prohibition, and 'khallid' means eternal, without end. Then 'sultanahu' is explained as his dominance over enemies. 'Wa a‘li' (and raise) means to execute his word and elevate his stature (shān) and his helpers (a‘wān). The term 'shān' is glossed as rank, and 'a‘wān' as supporters, whether from his own faction or not. 'Jayshahu' (his army) refers to his troops, and the phrase is syntactically related to 'khallid' or is a circumstantial qualifier. Finally, 'dā’imah' (lasting) means continuous, and 'qā’imah' (enduring) also means perpetual. This is a straightforward lexical and grammatical commentary on the prayer.

Key Terms
خلد (khallada): Made eternal
ملك (mulk): Authority over subjects
سلطان (sulṭān): Domination over enemies
شأن (sha'n): Stature, rank

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The commentator's lexical and grammatical analysis reveals that each term in the prayer is carefully chosen to request specific blessings: eternal authority, dominance, elevated stature, and perpetual support.

The Metaphor of Gilding: Why the Commentary is Called 'al-Tadhheeb'
Commentator explains the title metaphorically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the metaphorical relationship between a commentary and its matn as illustrated by the title 'al-Tadhheeb'.

Core Idea
A commentary is gold plating that adorns the pure silver of the matn.

In the Islamic scholarly tradition, commentators often choose titles that reflect the relationship between their work and the original text. This lesson explores the metaphor behind the title 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb', where the matn is likened to pure silver and the commentary to its gilding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and its components
The title is 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb'. First, parse each word: 'al-Tadhheeb' means gilding, 'fi' can mean 'in' or 'for', 'Sharh' means commentary, 'al-Tahzeeb' is the name of the original text. Note the literal meaning: 'The Gilding in Commentary on al-Tahzeeb'.
The commentator explains possible meanings of 'fi' (either 'for' or locative).
2
Understand the metaphor
The commentator defines 'al-tadhheeb' as the plating of silver with gold. This is not just decoration; it enhances and protects. The commentary does the same for the matn.
Gold plating is a process that adds value and beauty to an already pure substance.
3
Relate the metaphor to the matn
The matn is called 'al-Tahzeeb', meaning refinement or purification from filler. The commentator says it is 'like pure silver'. So the matn is already refined and valuable. The commentary is not fixing flaws but adding luster.
The matn's purity is assumed; the commentary's role is to make it shine.
4
Appreciate the adornment
The commentary adds beauty, clarity, and accessibility, just as gold plating makes silver objects more attractive. This metaphor is common in sharh literature, where titles often reflect the commentator's sense of their work's purpose.
Examples: 'Fath al-Bari' (opening) for Ibn Hajar; 'al-Tafsir al-Kabir' (great) for al-Razi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسَلْطَنَة قائمة، وقدر منيع، وشأن رفيع . وسميته بـ (التذهيب في شرح التهذيب راجياً من الله تعالى أن يكتسي مِن مَيَامِن قَبُولِه يمْنَةَ الإقبال، ويرتدي الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مَنيع ) أي : مانع من دخول النقص فيه . (قَوْلُهُ : وَشَأْنِ رَفِيعِ) أي : قَدْرٍ مُرتفع عن وقوع النقص فيه، فالفقرتان بمعنى . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَمَّيْتُهُ) عطف على قوله : شرحتُه . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّذْهِيب) هو إطلاءُ الفضَّةِ بالذهب، وقوله: في شرح ؛ أي: لشرح؛ أي : لكشف وإيضاح، ففي بمعنى اللام، أو أنَّها باقية على حالها، وفي الكلام حينئذ استعارة تبعية، وعلى كلا الاحتمالين فهو مُتعلّق بمحذوف صفة للتذهيب. وقولُهُ: (التَهذيب) ، أي : التّخليص من الحشو والتَّطويل، والمراد المهذّبُ والمخلّصُ مِمَّا ذكر، ففي كلام الشارح إشارة إلى أنَّ المَثْنَ كَأَنَّهُ فَضَّةٌ خالصة، وهذا الشَّرحُ طلاة له، ويُحتمل أنَّ قوله : في شرح حال من فاعل سمَّى؛ أي : في حال شرحي للتهذيب، وهذا كله بالنَّظرِ لهذا التركيب في حدّ ذاتِهِ قبل جعلِهِ عَلَماً على هذا الشرح، أمَّا بعد جعلِهِ عَلَماً له ؛ فتلك الكلمات لا معنى لها ؛ لأنَّها حينئذٍ بمنزلة حروفِ زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِياً) حال من فاعل سمَّى . (قَوْلُهُ : أَنْ يَكْتَسِيَ) أي: هذا الشَّرحُ . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَيَامِن أي بركاتِ جمع: يمن(۱)؛ أي: بركة. ) : (قَوْلُهُ : قَبُوْلِهِ) أي : قَبُولِ ذلكَ السُّلطان، وقَبُولُ الشَّيء : الرّضا به. (قَوْلُهُ : يَمْنَةَ الْإقْبَالِ) أي : يمنة هي الإقبال ؛ أي: إقبال السلطان عليه، والإقبال على الشَّيء ؛ التَّوجه إليه، وهذا بعضُ ثمراتِ قَبُولِهِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَيَرْتَدِيَ) أي : هذا الشَّرح . (۱) قوله: جمع يمن على غير قياس والقياس جمعه على أفعال كقفل وأقفال إلا أنه يلتبس بأيمان جمع يمين . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
And an enduring sultanate, an unassailable power, and an exalted status. And I named it 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb', hoping from Allah Almighty that it may clothe itself from the blessings of its acceptance with the right hand of favor, and that it may wear... al-Dasuqi (His statement: 'manee‘' means preventing the entry of deficiency into it. (His statement: 'and an exalted status' means a rank elevated above the occurrence of deficiency, so the two phrases are synonymous. (His statement: 'and I named it' is coordinated with his statement: 'I commented'. (His statement: 'bi al-tadhheeb' is the plating of silver with gold. And his statement: 'fi sharh' means 'for a commentary', i.e., for explanation and clarification; so 'fi' is in the sense of 'li', or it remains as it is, in which case there is a subsidiary metaphor. On both possibilities, it is related to an omitted description of 'al-tadhheeb'. And his statement: 'al-tahzeeb' means purification from padding and prolixity; what is meant is the refined and purified from what was mentioned. So in the commentator's words there is an indication that the matn is like pure silver, and this commentary is its plating. And it is possible that his statement: 'fi sharh' is a circumstantial qualifier from the subject of 'samma'; i.e., while I was commenting on al-Tahzeeb. And all this is with regard to this composition in itself before making it a proper name for this commentary. As for after making it a proper name, those words have no meaning, because then they are like the letters of 'Zaid'. (His statement: 'hoping' is a circumstantial qualifier from the subject of 'samma'. (His statement: 'that it may clothe itself' i.e., this commentary. (His statement: 'from the blessings' means barakat, plural of yumn; i.e., blessing. (His statement: 'its acceptance' means acceptance by that Sultan; acceptance of a thing is being pleased with it. (His statement: 'the right hand of favor' means favor is the turning towards; i.e., the Sultan's turning towards it. And turning towards a thing means directing oneself to it; this is some of the fruits of his acceptance. (His statement: 'and that it may wear' i.e., this commentary. (Footnote: His statement: 'jama‘ yumn' is irregular; the regular plural is aqfal-like, but it would be confused with ayman, plural of yameen.)
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter explanation of the title of the commentary. It begins with the last part of the original praise: 'an enduring sultanate, an unassailable power, and an exalted status.' Then the commentator states the title: 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb.' He then comments on each phrase. First, 'manee‘' (unassailable) means it prevents deficiency from entering. 'Sha‘n rafee‘' (exalted status) also means a rank free from deficiency; the two are synonymous. Then he explains the naming: 'wa sammaytuhu' is coordinated with 'sharaltuhu' (I commented). 'Bi al-tadhheeb' is the act of plating silver with gold. The phrase 'fi sharh' could mean 'for a commentary' (fi in the sense of li) or remains locative, implying a subsidiary metaphor. As for 'al-tahzeeb', it means purification from filler and length, and the intended meaning is the refined text. The commentator suggests that the original matn is like pure silver, and this commentary is its gold plating, thus the name 'al-Tadhheeb'. He also considers that 'fi sharh' might be a circumstantial qualifier ('while I was commenting'). He notes that this analysis applies to the phrase in itself before it became a proper name. Once it became a proper name (like 'Zaid'), the individual words lose their independent meaning. Then he continues explaining the phrase 'rajian' hoping, which is a circumstantial qualifier, and then explains the clause 'an yaktasi min mayamin qabulihi yumnat al-iqbal' (that it may clothe itself from the blessings of its acceptance with the right hand of favor). He glosses 'mayamin' as blessings (barakat), plural of yumn. 'Qabul' (acceptance) means the Sultan's acceptance. 'Yumnat al-iqbal' (the right hand of favor) means the favor itself, i.e., the Sultan's turning towards the book. This is a fruit of acceptance. Finally, 'wa yartadi' (and that it may wear) also refers to the commentary. The footnote discusses the irregular plural of 'yumn'. This passage combines grammatical, lexical, and rhetorical explanation of the title and the author's intention.

التهذيب
شرح

D) Iron

Key Takeaway
The title 'al-Tadhheeb' poetically conveys that a commentary adorns and elevates the matn, just as gold plating beautifies silver.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
From Composite Phrase to Proper Name: The Semantic Shift in 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb'
Commentator discusses the proper name status of the title

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the literal meaning of a composite phrase and its function as a proper name ('alam) in Islamic scholarly texts.

Core Idea
Once a phrase becomes a proper name, its individual words lose their independent meanings.

The commentator notes that before the title 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb' became a proper name for his work, one could analyze its parts. But after it became a proper name, those words function like the letters in 'Zaid'—they no longer carry their separate lexical meanings. This lesson examines this important linguistic principle that recurs in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the commentator's remark
He says: 'This is with regard to this composition in itself before making it a proper name. As for after making it a proper name, those words have no meaning; they are like the letters of 'Zaid'.'
The commentator draws a stark contrast: prior to being a proper name, the title is a meaningful description; afterwards, it is purely denotative.
2
Understand the concept of 'alam
In Arabic grammar and logic, a proper name ('alam) is a noun that designates a specific entity without describing its attributes. For example, 'Zaid' does not mean 'growth' but identifies a person. Once assigned, the original descriptive meaning (if any) is irrelevant for reference.
Many proper names originate as descriptions but then shift to pure reference.
3
Apply to the title
Initially, 'al-Tadhheeb fi Sharh al-Tahzeeb' literally meant 'The Gilding in Commentary on al-Tahzeeb'. But as a title of this specific commentary, it simply names the book. The words 'tadhheeb', 'sharh', 'tahzeeb' no longer individually signify gilding, commentary, or refinement in the context of the title.
The commentator emphasizes that the linguistic analysis he just gave applies only when the phrase is not yet a proper name.
4
Recognize the principle in other Islamic texts
Many technical terms in Islamic sciences began as descriptive phrases and then became proper names. For example: 'Ilm al-Kalam' originally meant 'the science of speech' (kalam meaning speech), but now it is the proper name for a specific theological discipline. Similarly, 'al-Fiqh' originally meant 'understanding' but now denotes Islamic jurisprudence.
This shift is common and understanding it avoids misinterpretation.

(قَوْلُهُ : وَشَأْنِ رَفِيعِ) أي : قَدْرٍ مُرتفع عن وقوع النقص فيه، فالفقرتان بمعنى . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَمَّيْتُهُ) عطف على قوله : شرحتُه . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّذْهِيب) هو إطلاءُ الفضَّةِ بالذهب، وقوله: في شرح ؛ أي: لشرح؛ أي : لكشف وإيضاح، ففي بمعنى اللام، أو أنَّها باقية على حالها، وفي الكلام حينئذ استعارة تبعية، وعلى كلا الاحتمالين فهو مُتعلّق بمحذوف صفة للتذهيب. وقولُهُ: (التَهذيب) ، أي : التّخليص من الحشو والتَّطويل، والمراد المهذّبُ والمخلّصُ مِمَّا ذكر، ففي كلام الشارح إشارة إلى أنَّ المَثْنَ كَأَنَّهُ فَضَّةٌ خالصة، وهذا الشَّرحُ طلاة له، ويُحتمل أنَّ قوله : في شرح حال من فاعل سمَّى؛ أي : في حال شرحي للتهذيب، وهذا كله بالنَّظرِ لهذا التركيب في حدّ ذاتِهِ قبل جعلِهِ عَلَماً على هذا الشرح، أمَّا بعد جعلِهِ عَلَماً له ؛ فتلك الكلمات لا معنى لها ؛ لأنَّها حينئذٍ بمنزلة حروفِ زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِياً) حال من فاعل سمَّى . (قَوْلُهُ : أَنْ يَكْتَسِيَ) أي: هذا الشَّرحُ . Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Title's Metaphor: Tadhheeb and Tahdhīb
Al-Dasuqi explains the title's etymology and metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the metaphorical relationship between the commentary's title 'al-Tadhheeb' and the original matn 'al-Tahdhīb', and identify the literal meaning of the term.

Core Idea
A title can be a metaphor that reveals the author's intent.

In this lesson, we examine how al-Dasuqi unpacks the title of his commentary. He shows that 'al-Tadhheeb' (gilding) literally means coating silver with gold, and that the matn 'al-Tahdhīb' (purification) is like pure silver. This metaphor highlights the commentary's role in enhancing the original.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Find 'التذهيب' and 'التهذيب' in the Arabic. Note their linguistic roots.
2
Understand the literal meaning of 'التذهيب'
Al-Dasuqi says it is 'إطلاء الفضة بالذهب' – coating silver with gold. This implies the original has value (silver) and the commentary adds further value (gold).
3
Understand the metaphor
The commentator says the matn is like pure silver, and the commentary is its plating. The commentary does not replace the original but beautifies and enhances it.
4
Consider the effect of proper noun status
Al-Dasuqi notes that once 'التذهيب' becomes a proper name, the individual words lose their lexical meaning. This distinction is important because it shows the shift from descriptive to nominative function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مَنيع ) أي : مانع من دخول النقص فيه . (قَوْلُهُ : وَشَأْنِ رَفِيعِ) أي : قَدْرٍ مُرتفع عن وقوع النقص فيه، فالفقرتان بمعنى . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَمَّيْتُهُ) عطف على قوله : شرحتُه . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّذْهِيب) هو إطلاءُ الفضَّةِ بالذهب، وقوله: في شرح ؛ أي: لشرح؛ أي : لكشف وإيضاح، ففي بمعنى اللام، أو أنَّها باقية على حالها، وفي الكلام حينئذ استعارة تبعية، وعلى كلا الاحتمالين فهو مُتعلّق بمحذوف صفة للتذهيب. وقولُهُ: (التَهذيب) ، أي : التّخليص من الحشو والتَّطويل، والمراد المهذّبُ والمخلّصُ مِمَّا ذكر، ففي كلام الشارح إشارة إلى أنَّ المَثْنَ كَأَنَّهُ فَضَّةٌ خالصة، وهذا الشَّرحُ طلاة له، ويُحتمل أنَّ قوله : في شرح حال من فاعل سمَّى؛ أي : في حال شرحي للتهذيب، وهذا كله بالنَّظرِ لهذا التركيب في حدّ ذاتِهِ قبل جعلِهِ عَلَماً على هذا الشرح، أمَّا بعد جعلِهِ عَلَماً له ؛ فتلك الكلمات لا معنى لها ؛ لأنَّها حينئذٍ بمنزلة حروفِ زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِياً) حال من فاعل سمَّى . (قَوْلُهُ : أَنْ يَكْتَسِيَ) أي: هذا الشَّرحُ . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَيَامِن) أي بركاتِ جمع: يمن(۱)؛ أي: بركة. ) : (قَوْلُهُ : قَبُوْلِهِ) أي : قَبُولِ ذلكَ السُّلطان، وقَبُولُ الشَّيء : الرّضا به. (قَوْلُهُ : يَمْنَةَ الْإقْبَالِ) أي : يمنة هي الإقبال ؛ أي: إقبال السلطان عليه، والإقبال على الشَّيء ؛ التَّوجه إليه، وهذا بعضُ ثمراتِ قَبُولِهِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَيَرْتَدِيَ) أي : هذا الشَّرح . العطار (۱) قوله: جمع يمن على غير قياس والقياس جمعه على أفعال كقفل وأقفال إلا أنه يلتبس بأيمان جمع يمين . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.  الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَلَامِحِ جَمعُ مَلْمَح، بمعنى لمح؛ وهو النَّظر بطرف خفي . (قَوْلُهُ : نَظَرِهِ) أي: نظرِ السُّلطان إليه، ومن في قوله: من ملامح؛ للتعليل، أو ابتدائية، وفيها معنى التبعيض، وقوله : برداء العزّ ; أي: بالعزّ والجمالِ الشَّبيهين بالرداء . (قَوْلُهُ : إِنَّ اللَّهَ) أي : إِنَّما رجوتُ مِنَ اللهِ دونَ غيرِهِ قَبُولَ السُّلطانِ له؛ لأنَّ اللَّهَ وليُّ ; أَي مَوْلَى; أي: مُعطي. (قَوْلُهُ: وَبِتَحْقِيقِ) أي : إثباتِ وتحصيل والجار والمجرور متعلق بتحقيق(۱)، والأُمنية : مَا يَتمنَّاهُ الإنسان; أي: وحقيق بإثبات وتحصيل أُمنيتي; أي: ما تمنيتُهُ مِن قَبُولِ السُّلطانِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا) إدخالُ هاء التَّنبيه على ضميرِ الرَّفعِ المخبرِ عنه بغيرِ اسمِ العطار (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا أَشْرَعُ فِيهِ إِدْخَالُ هَا التَّنبيه على ضمير رفعِ مُنفَصِلِ; خَبَرُهُ ليسَ اسم إشارة، وقد وقع في كلام ابني مالك وهِشَام استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ مع تصريحهما كغيرهما بشذوذه في نحو قول الشاعر : أَبَا حَكَم هَا أَنتَ نَجْمٌ مُجَالِدٌ ووَجهُهُ أَنَّ هَا التَّنبيه إنَّما تلحَقُ اسم الإشارة، فإذا لَحِقَت غيره ولكن وقع الخبر عنه اسم إشارةٍ; كان كأنَّها لم تُفارقه ; لأنَّ المبتدأ الذي دخلت عليه عين الخبر، فكأَنَّها دَخَلَت على اسم الإشارة، وفي الرِّضَى، وما حُكِيَ عن الزمخشري مِن قولهم : هَا إِنَّ زيداً منطلَقٌ، وها أنا أفعلُ كذا ; مِمَّا لم أعثر له على شاهد .ا.هـ. وقال أبو حيان في الارتشاف : قالَ الزَّجَاجُ : الأكثرُ والأحسَنُ أن(٢) يستعمل ها المضمر، ولو قلتَ : هَا زِيدٌ ذَا; جازَ بِلَا خِلَاف .
Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'manī‘') i.e., preventing imperfection from entering it. (His saying: 'and a lofty station') i.e., a high degree above the occurrence of imperfection in it, so the two phrases have the same meaning. (His saying: 'and I named it') is conjuncted to his saying: 'I explained it'. (His saying: 'with al-Tadhheeb') it is the coating of silver with gold, and his saying: 'in Sharh' i.e., for Sharh; i.e., for unveiling and clarifying, so 'fī' is in the meaning of the lām, or that it remains in its original state, and in the speech then there is a subsidiary metaphor, and on both possibilities it is attached to a deleted adjective for al-Tadhheeb. And his saying: (al-Tahdhīb), i.e., purification from filler and prolixity, and the intended meaning is the purified and purified from what was mentioned, so in the speech of the commentator there is an indication that the matn is like pure silver, and this commentary is its plating. And it is possible that his saying: 'fī sharh' is a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'sammā', i.e., in the state of my explaining al-Tahdhīb. And all of this is with regard to this composition in itself before making it a proper noun for this commentary. But after making it a proper noun for it, then those words have no meaning, because they are then like the letters of Zayd. (His saying: 'rājiyan') is a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'sammā'. (His saying: 'an yaktasiya') i.e., this commentary. (His saying: 'min mayāmin') i.e., blessings, plural of yumn; i.e., blessing. (His saying: 'qabūlihi') i.e., acceptance of that Sultan, and acceptance of a thing is approval of it. (His saying: 'yamnata al-iqbāl') i.e., yumnah is al-iqbāl; i.e., the Sultan's turning towards it, and al-iqbāl 'alā al-shay' is turning towards it, and this is some of the fruits of his acceptance of it. (His saying: 'wa yartadiya') i.e., this commentary. Al-‘Aṭṭār: (1) His saying: plural of yumn anomalously, and the analogical plural is on af‘āl like qufl and aqfāl, except that it would be confused with aymān plural of yamīn. End quote from al-Sharnūbī. [Page 79] Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'min malāmiḥ') plural of malmaḥ, meaning lamḥ; which is looking with a stealthy glance. (His saying: 'naẓarihi') i.e., the Sultan's looking at it, and 'min' in his saying: 'min malāmiḥ' is for causation, or inchoative, and in it is the meaning of partiality, and his saying: 'bi-ridā’ al-‘izzi' i.e., with the might and beauty resembling a garment. (His saying: 'inna Allāha') i.e., I only hoped from Allah, not other than Him, for the Sultan's acceptance of it, because Allah is waliyy; i.e., mawlā; i.e., giver. (His saying: 'wa bi-tahqīqi') i.e., establishing and attaining, and the preposition and its object are attached to 'taḥqīq' (1), and al-umniyyah is what one wishes; i.e., and it is fitting for establishing and attaining my wish; i.e., what I wished for from the Sultan's acceptance of it. (His saying: 'wa hā ana') is the insertion of the interjection hā onto a detached nominative pronoun whose predicate is not a demonstrative noun. Al-‘Aṭṭār: (His saying: 'wa hā ana ashra‘u fīhi') is the insertion of hā of attention onto a detached nominative pronoun; its predicate is not a demonstrative noun, and it has occurred in the speech of Ibn Mālik and Hishām using it like that just like that, despite their stating, like others, its irregularity in like the poet's saying: 'O Abā Ḥakam, hā anta a star of valour.' And its justification is that hā of attention only attaches to the demonstrative noun, but when it attaches to other than it but the predicate is a demonstrative noun, it is as if it did not leave it, because the subject it entered is the same as the predicate, so it is as if it entered the demonstrative noun. And in al-Riḍā, and what is reported from al-Zamakhsharī from their saying: 'hā inna Zaydan muntaliqun', and 'hā ana af‘alu kadhā', that which I have not found a witness for. End quote. And Abū Ḥayyān in al-Irtishāf said: al-Zajjāj said: the more frequent and better is that (2) one uses hā with a pronoun, and if you say: 'hā Zaydun dhā', it is allowed without disagreement.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a detailed gloss by al-Dasuqi and al-‘Aṭṭār on the author's preface. It functions as an expansion probe, clarifying the words of the original commentator. The commentary proceeds line by line. First, al-Dasuqi explains the terms 'manī‘' (preventive) and 'sha’n rafī‘' (lofty station), noting they are synonymous. Then he discusses the title 'al-Tadhheeb' (gilding) and its relation to 'al-Tahdhīb' (purification). He notes that 'tadhheeb' literally means coating silver with gold, metaphorically indicating that the commentary enhances the matn like gold plating pure silver. He also analyzes the grammar of 'fī sharh', suggesting it could mean 'for the commentary' (with fī in the sense of lām) or as a circumstantial accusative ('in the state of explaining'). He emphasizes that before the phrase became a proper name, these linguistic considerations apply, but after naming, the words lose their lexical meaning. Next, he explains 'rājiyan' as a circumstantial accusative, and clarifies that 'yaktasī' refers to the commentary being adorned. He parses 'mayāmin' as a plural of 'yumn' (blessing), with a note from al-‘Aṭṭār on its anomalous plural form. 'Qabūl' means approval by the Sultan. 'Yamnah al-iqbāl' is equated with the Sultan's turning towards the work. The phrase 'wa yartadiya' again refers to the commentary being clothed in the garment of glory. Al-Dasuqi then moves to 'min malāmiḥ', explaining it as glances or aspects, and the attached 'min' indicates causation or source. 'Naẓarihi' is the Sultan's gaze. 'Bi-ridā’ al-‘izzi' is a metaphor for might and beauty. For 'inna Allāha', he stresses that hope is only from Allah, who is the Giver. 'Bi-tahqīq' means actualizing the wish for acceptance. Finally, al-‘Aṭṭār provides a lengthy grammatical note on the construction 'hā ana' (lo! I). He discusses its irregularity because hā usually attaches to demonstratives, but when the predicate is a demonstrative (like 'hā anta dhā'), it is acceptable. He cites authorities like Ibn Mālik, Hishām, al-Zamakhsharī, and Abū Ḥayyān, showing that this usage, while rare, has precedents in Arabic. This grammatical excursus demonstrates the author's philological rigor.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Grammar of 'fī sharh': Two Interpretations
Al-Dasuqi analyses the grammar of 'fī sharh'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the two grammatical interpretations of the prepositional phrase 'fī sharh' as analysed by al-Dasuqi.

Core Idea
A single prepositional phrase can have multiple valid analyses in classical Arabic.

Al-Dasuqi discusses the phrase 'fī sharh' appearing after the verb 'sammaytu'. He presents two possibilities: 'fī' could mean 'for' (lām), or it could remain in its original sense of 'in', leading to a circumstantial clause. This lesson will walk you through both interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Locate the phrase
Find 'في شرح' (fī sharh) in the Arabic in the context of 'بالتذهيب في شرح التهذيب'.
2
First interpretation: 'fī' as lām
Al-Dasuqi says 'fī' could be in the sense of lām, meaning 'for'. Then 'fī sharh' means 'for the commentary', i.e., the name is given for the purpose of commentary.
3
Second interpretation: 'fī' as circumstantial
Alternatively, 'fī' retains its original meaning 'in', making 'fī sharh' a circumstantial accusative (ḥāl) meaning 'in the state of explaining al-Tahdhīb'.
4
Note the consequence
On both readings, the phrase attaches to a deleted adjective describing 'al-Tadhheeb'. In the second interpretation, a subsidiary metaphor (istiʿāra tabaʿiyya) arises.
5
Distinguish pre- and post-naming
Al-Dasuqi emphasizes that these analyses apply only before the title became a proper noun. After naming, the words are just part of the name and lack lexical meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مَنيع ) أي : مانع من دخول النقص فيه . (قَوْلُهُ : وَشَأْنِ رَفِيعِ) أي : قَدْرٍ مُرتفع عن وقوع النقص فيه، فالفقرتان بمعنى . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَمَّيْتُهُ) عطف على قوله : شرحتُه . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّذْهِيب) هو إطلاءُ الفضَّةِ بالذهب، وقوله: في شرح ؛ أي: لشرح؛ أي : لكشف وإيضاح، ففي بمعنى اللام، أو أنَّها باقية على حالها، وفي الكلام حينئذ استعارة تبعية، وعلى كلا الاحتمالين فهو مُتعلّق بمحذوف صفة للتذهيب. وقولُهُ: (التَهذيب) ، أي : التّخليص من الحشو والتَّطويل، والمراد المهذّبُ والمخلّصُ مِمَّا ذكر، ففي كلام الشارح إشارة إلى أنَّ المَثْنَ كَأَنَّهُ فَضَّةٌ خالصة، وهذا الشَّرحُ طلاة له، ويُحتمل أنَّ قوله : في شرح حال من فاعل سمَّى؛ أي : في حال شرحي للتهذيب، وهذا كله بالنَّظرِ لهذا التركيب في حدّ ذاتِهِ قبل جعلِهِ عَلَماً على هذا الشرح، أمَّا بعد جعلِهِ عَلَماً له ؛ فتلك الكلمات لا معنى لها ؛ لأنَّها حينئذٍ بمنزلة حروفِ زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِياً) حال من فاعل سمَّى . (قَوْلُهُ : أَنْ يَكْتَسِيَ) أي: هذا الشَّرحُ . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَيَامِن) أي بركاتِ جمع: يمن(۱)؛ أي: بركة. ) : (قَوْلُهُ : قَبُوْلِهِ) أي : قَبُولِ ذلكَ السُّلطان، وقَبُولُ الشَّيء : الرّضا به. (قَوْلُهُ : يَمْنَةَ الْإقْبَالِ) أي : يمنة هي الإقبال ؛ أي: إقبال السلطان عليه، والإقبال على الشَّيء ؛ التَّوجه إليه، وهذا بعضُ ثمراتِ قَبُولِهِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَيَرْتَدِيَ) أي : هذا الشَّرح . العطار (۱) قوله: جمع يمن على غير قياس والقياس جمعه على أفعال كقفل وأقفال إلا أنه يلتبس بأيمان جمع يمين . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.  الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَلَامِحِ جَمعُ مَلْمَح، بمعنى لمح؛ وهو النَّظر بطرف خفي . (قَوْلُهُ : نَظَرِهِ) أي: نظرِ السُّلطان إليه، ومن في قوله: من ملامح؛ للتعليل، أو ابتدائية، وفيها معنى التبعيض، وقوله : برداء العزّ ; أي: بالعزّ والجمالِ الشَّبيهين بالرداء . (قَوْلُهُ: وَبِتَحْقِيقِ) أي : إثباتِ وتحصيل والجار والمجرور متعلق بتحقيق(۱)، والأُمنية : مَا يَتمنَّاهُ الإنسان; أي: وحقيق بإثبات وتحصيل أُمنيتي; أي: ما تمنيتُهُ مِن قَبُولِ السُّلطانِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا) إدخالُ هاء التَّنبيه على ضميرِ الرَّفعِ المخبرِ عنه بغيرِ اسمِ العطار (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا أَشْرَعُ فِيهِ إِدْخَالُ هَا التَّنبيه على ضمير رفعِ مُنفَصِلِ; خَبَرُهُ ليسَ اسم إشارة، وقد وقع في كلام ابني مالك وهِشَام استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ مع تصريحهما كغيرهما بشذوذه في نحو قول الشاعر : أَبَا حَكَم هَا أَنتَ نَجْمٌ مُجَالِدٌ ووَجهُهُ أَنَّ هَا التَّنبيه إنَّما تلحَقُ اسم الإشارة، فإذا لَحِقَت غيره ولكن وقع الخبر عنه اسم إشارةٍ; كان كأنَّها لم تُفارقه ; لأنَّ المبتدأ الذي دخلت عليه عين الخبر، فكأَنَّها دَخَلَت على اسم الإشارة، وفي الرِّضَى، وما حُكِيَ عن الزمخشري مِن قولهم : هَا إِنَّ زيداً منطلَقٌ، وها أنا أفعلُ كذا ; مِمَّا لم أعثر له على شاهد .ا.هـ. وقال أبو حيان في الارتشاف : قالَ الزَّجَاجُ : الأكثرُ والأحسَنُ أن(٢) يستعمل ها المضمر، ولو قلتَ : هَا زِيدٌ ذَا; جازَ بِلَا خِلَاف .

Commentary
This passage is a detailed gloss by al-Dasuqi and al-‘Aṭṭār on the author's preface. It functions as an expansion probe, clarifying the words of the original commentator. The commentary proceeds line by line. First, al-Dasuqi explains the terms 'manī‘' (preventive) and 'sha’n rafī‘' (lofty station), noting they are synonymous. Then he discusses the title 'al-Tadhheeb' (gilding) and its relation to 'al-Tahdhīb' (purification). He notes that 'tadhheeb' literally means coating silver with gold, metaphorically indicating that the commentary enhances the matn like gold plating pure silver. He also analyzes the grammar of 'fī sharh', suggesting it could mean 'for the commentary' (with fī in the sense of lām) or as a circumstantial accusative ('in the state of explaining'). He emphasizes that before the phrase became a proper name, these linguistic considerations apply, but after naming, the words lose their lexical meaning. Next, he explains 'rājiyan' as a circumstantial accusative, and clarifies that 'yaktasī' refers to the commentary being adorned. He parses 'mayāmin' as a plural of 'yumn' (blessing), with a note from al-‘Aṭṭār on its anomalous plural form. 'Qabūl' means approval by the Sultan. 'Yamnah al-iqbāl' is equated with the Sultan's turning towards the work. The phrase 'wa yartadiya' again refers to the commentary being clothed in the garment of glory. Al-Dasuqi then moves to 'min malāmiḥ', explaining it as glances or aspects, and the attached 'min' indicates causation or source. 'Naẓarihi' is the Sultan's gaze. 'Bi-ridā’ al-‘izzi' is a metaphor for might and beauty. For 'inna Allāha', he stresses that hope is only from Allah, who is the Giver. 'Bi-tahqīq' means actualizing the wish for acceptance. Finally, al-‘Aṭṭār provides a lengthy grammatical note on the construction 'hā ana' (lo! I). He discusses its irregularity because hā usually attaches to demonstratives, but when the predicate is a demonstrative (like 'hā anta dhā'), it is acceptable. He cites authorities like Ibn Mālik, Hishām, al-Zamakhsharī, and Abū Ḥayyān, showing that this usage, while rare, has precedents in Arabic. This grammatical excursus demonstrates the author's philological rigor.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
5 min
The Construction 'Hā Ana': When Interjection Meets Pronoun
Al-‘Aṭṭār glosses the grammatical construction 'hā ana'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rule for using the interjection 'hā' with detached pronouns and justify its irregular usage when the predicate is a demonstrative.

Core Idea
Even irregular grammatical constructions can be justified by analogy.

Al-‘Aṭṭār provides a detailed grammatical note on the phrase 'hā ana' (lo! I) used by the commentator. He explains that 'hā' of attention normally attaches to demonstrative nouns, but here it attaches to a pronoun. This lesson unpacks his justification based on the predicate being a demonstrative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the construction
Find 'ها أنا' in the Arabic and note that the predicate is not a demonstrative (here it is 'أشرع فيه').
2
Understand the general rule
'Hā' of attention (hā al-tanbīh) normally attaches to demonstrative nouns, e.g., 'hā dhā'.
3
Recognize the irregularity
Attaching 'hā' to a pronoun is considered shādhdh (irregular) by grammarians like Ibn Mālik and Hishām.
4
Learn the justification
If the predicate of the pronoun is a demonstrative, then it is as if 'hā' attached to that demonstrative because the subject and predicate are the same entity. Example: 'hā anta dhā'. Al-‘Aṭṭār cites authorities like al-Zamakhsharī who allow it.
5
Note the authorities
Al-‘Aṭṭār cites al-Zamakhsharī, Abū Ḥayyān, and al-Zajjāj, who confirm the permissibility of using 'hā' with pronouns, especially when a demonstrative is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مَنيع ) أي : مانع من دخول النقص فيه . (قَوْلُهُ : وَشَأْنِ رَفِيعِ) أي : قَدْرٍ مُرتفع عن وقوع النقص فيه، فالفقرتان بمعنى . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَمَّيْتُهُ) عطف على قوله : شرحتُه . (قَوْلُهُ : بِالتَّذْهِيب) هو إطلاءُ الفضَّةِ بالذهب، وقوله: في شرح ؛ أي: لشرح؛ أي : لكشف وإيضاح، ففي بمعنى اللام، أو أنَّها باقية على حالها، وفي الكلام حينئذ استعارة تبعية، وعلى كلا الاحتمالين فهو مُتعلّق بمحذوف صفة للتذهيب. وقولُهُ: (التَهذيب) ، أي : التّخليص من الحشو والتَّطويل، والمراد المهذّبُ والمخلّصُ مِمَّا ذكر، ففي كلام الشارح إشارة إلى أنَّ المَثْنَ كَأَنَّهُ فَضَّةٌ خالصة، وهذا الشَّرحُ طلاة له، ويُحتمل أنَّ قوله : في شرح حال من فاعل سمَّى؛ أي : في حال شرحي للتهذيب، وهذا كله بالنَّظرِ لهذا التركيب في حدّ ذاتِهِ قبل جعلِهِ عَلَماً على هذا الشرح، أمَّا بعد جعلِهِ عَلَماً له ؛ فتلك الكلمات لا معنى لها ؛ لأنَّها حينئذٍ بمنزلة حروفِ زيد . (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِياً) حال من فاعل سمَّى . (قَوْلُهُ : أَنْ يَكْتَسِيَ) أي: هذا الشَّرحُ . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَيَامِن) أي بركاتِ جمع: يمن(۱)؛ أي: بركة. ) : (قَوْلُهُ : قَبُوْلِهِ) أي : قَبُولِ ذلكَ السُّلطان، وقَبُولُ الشَّيء : الرّضا به. (قَوْلُهُ : يَمْنَةَ الْإقْبَالِ) أي : يمنة هي الإقبال ؛ أي: إقبال السلطان عليه، والإقبال على الشَّيء ؛ التَّوجه إليه، وهذا بعضُ ثمراتِ قَبُولِهِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَيَرْتَدِيَ) أي : هذا الشَّرح . العطار (۱) قوله: جمع يمن على غير قياس والقياس جمعه على أفعال كقفل وأقفال إلا أنه يلتبس بأيمان جمع يمين . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.  الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ مَلَامِحِ جَمعُ مَلْمَح، بمعنى لمح؛ وهو النَّظر بطرف خفي . (قَوْلُهُ : نَظَرِهِ) أي: نظرِ السُّلطان إليه، ومن في قوله: من ملامح؛ للتعليل، أو ابتدائية، وفيها معنى التبعيض، وقوله : برداء العزّ ; أي: بالعزّ والجمالِ الشَّبيهين بالرداء . (قَوْلُهُ : إِنَّ اللَّهَ) أي : إِنَّما رجوتُ مِنَ اللهِ دونَ غيرِهِ قَبُولَ السُّلطانِ له؛ لأنَّ اللَّهَ وليُّ ; أَي مَوْلَى; أي: مُعطي. (قَوْلُهُ: وَبِتَحْقِيقِ) أي : إثباتِ وتحصيل والجار والمجرور متعلق بتحقيق(۱)، والأُمنية : مَا يَتمنَّاهُ الإنسان; أي: وحقيق بإثبات وتحصيل أُمنيتي; أي: ما تمنيتُهُ مِن قَبُولِ السُّلطانِ له . (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا) إدخالُ هاء التَّنبيه على ضميرِ الرَّفعِ المخبرِ عنه بغيرِ اسمِ العطار (قَوْلُهُ : وَهَا أَنَا أَشْرَعُ فِيهِ إِدْخَالُ هَا التَّنبيه على ضمير رفعِ مُنفَصِلِ; خَبَرُهُ ليسَ اسم إشارة، وقد وقع في كلام ابني مالك وهِشَام استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ استعمالُهُ كُذلكَ مع تصريحهما كغيرهما بشذوذه في نحو قول الشاعر : أَبَا حَكَم هَا أَنتَ نَجْمٌ مُجَالِدٌ ووَجهُهُ أَنَّ هَا التَّنبيه إنَّما تلحَقُ اسم الإشارة، فإذا لَحِقَت غيره ولكن وقع الخبر عنه اسم إشارةٍ; كان كأنَّها لم تُفارقه ; لأنَّ المبتدأ الذي دخلت عليه عين الخبر، فكأَنَّها دَخَلَت على اسم الإشارة، وفي الرِّضَى، وما حُكِيَ عن الزمخشري مِن قولهم : هَا إِنَّ زيداً منطلَقٌ، وها أنا أفعلُ كذا ; مِمَّا لم أعثر له على شاهد .ا.هـ. وقال أبو حيان في الارتشاف : قالَ الزَّجَاجُ : الأكثرُ والأحسَنُ أن(٢) يستعمل ها المضمر، ولو قلتَ : هَا زِيدٌ ذَا; جازَ بِلَا خِلَاف .
Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'manī‘') i.e., preventing imperfection from entering it. (His saying: 'and a lofty station') i.e., a high degree above the occurrence of imperfection in it, so the two phrases have the same meaning. (His saying: 'and I named it') is conjuncted to his saying: 'I explained it'. (His saying: 'with al-Tadhheeb') it is the coating of silver with gold, and his saying: 'in Sharh' i.e., for Sharh; i.e., for unveiling and clarifying, so 'fī' is in the meaning of the lām, or that it remains in its original state, and in the speech then there is a subsidiary metaphor, and on both possibilities it is attached to a deleted adjective for al-Tadhheeb. And his saying: (al-Tahdhīb), i.e., purification from filler and prolixity, and the intended meaning is the purified and purified from what was mentioned, so in the speech of the commentator there is an indication that the matn is like pure silver, and this commentary is its plating. And it is possible that his saying: 'fī sharh' is a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'sammā', i.e., in the state of my explaining al-Tahdhīb. And all of this is with regard to this composition in itself before making it a proper noun for this commentary. But after making it a proper noun for it, then those words have no meaning, because they are then like the letters of Zayd. (His saying: 'rājiyan') is a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'sammā'. (His saying: 'an yaktasiya') i.e., this commentary. (His saying: 'min mayāmin') i.e., blessings, plural of yumn; i.e., blessing. (His saying: 'qabūlihi') i.e., acceptance of that Sultan, and acceptance of a thing is approval of it. (His saying: 'yamnata al-iqbāl') i.e., yumnah is al-iqbāl; i.e., the Sultan's turning towards it, and al-iqbāl 'alā al-shay' is turning towards it, and this is some of the fruits of his acceptance of it. (His saying: 'wa yartadiya') i.e., this commentary. Al-‘Aṭṭār: (1) His saying: plural of yumn anomalously, and the analogical plural is on af‘āl like qufl and aqfāl, except that it would be confused with aymān plural of yamīn. End quote from al-Sharnūbī. [Page 79] Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'min malāmiḥ') plural of malmaḥ, meaning lamḥ; which is looking with a stealthy glance. (His saying: 'naẓarihi') i.e., the Sultan's looking at it, and 'min' in his saying: 'min malāmiḥ' is for causation, or inchoative, and in it is the meaning of partiality, and his saying: 'bi-ridā’ al-‘izzi' i.e., with the might and beauty resembling a garment. (His saying: 'inna Allāha') i.e., I only hoped from Allah, not other than Him, for the Sultan's acceptance of it, because Allah is waliyy; i.e., mawlā; i.e., giver. (His saying: 'wa bi-tahqīqi') i.e., establishing and attaining, and the preposition and its object are attached to 'taḥqīq' (1), and al-umniyyah is what one wishes; i.e., and it is fitting for establishing and attaining my wish; i.e., what I wished for from the Sultan's acceptance of it. (His saying: 'wa hā ana') is the insertion of the interjection hā onto a detached nominative pronoun whose predicate is not a demonstrative noun. Al-‘Aṭṭār: (His saying: 'wa hā ana ashra‘u fīhi') is the insertion of hā of attention onto a detached nominative pronoun; its predicate is not a demonstrative noun, and it has occurred in the speech of Ibn Mālik and Hishām using it like that just like that, despite their stating, like others, its irregularity in like the poet's saying: 'O Abā Ḥakam, hā anta a star of valour.' And its justification is that hā of attention only attaches to the demonstrative noun, but when it attaches to other than it but the predicate is a demonstrative noun, it is as if it did not leave it, because the subject it entered is the same as the predicate, so it is as if it entered the demonstrative noun. And in al-Riḍā, and what is reported from al-Zamakhsharī from their saying: 'hā inna Zaydan muntaliqun', and 'hā ana af‘alu kadhā', that which I have not found a witness for. End quote. And Abū Ḥayyān in al-Irtishāf said: al-Zajjāj said: the more frequent and better is that (2) one uses hā with a pronoun, and if you say: 'hā Zaydun dhā', it is allowed without disagreement.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a detailed gloss by al-Dasuqi and al-‘Aṭṭār on the author's preface. It functions as an expansion probe, clarifying the words of the original commentator. The commentary proceeds line by line. First, al-Dasuqi explains the terms 'manī‘' (preventive) and 'sha’n rafī‘' (lofty station), noting they are synonymous. Then he discusses the title 'al-Tadhheeb' (gilding) and its relation to 'al-Tahdhīb' (purification). He notes that 'tadhheeb' literally means coating silver with gold, metaphorically indicating that the commentary enhances the matn like gold plating pure silver. He also analyzes the grammar of 'fī sharh', suggesting it could mean 'for the commentary' (with fī in the sense of lām) or as a circumstantial accusative ('in the state of explaining'). He emphasizes that before the phrase became a proper name, these linguistic considerations apply, but after naming, the words lose their lexical meaning. Next, he explains 'rājiyan' as a circumstantial accusative, and clarifies that 'yaktasī' refers to the commentary being adorned. He parses 'mayāmin' as a plural of 'yumn' (blessing), with a note from al-‘Aṭṭār on its anomalous plural form. 'Qabūl' means approval by the Sultan. 'Yamnah al-iqbāl' is equated with the Sultan's turning towards the work. The phrase 'wa yartadiya' again refers to the commentary being clothed in the garment of glory. Al-Dasuqi then moves to 'min malāmiḥ', explaining it as glances or aspects, and the attached 'min' indicates causation or source. 'Naẓarihi' is the Sultan's gaze. 'Bi-ridā’ al-‘izzi' is a metaphor for might and beauty. For 'inna Allāha', he stresses that hope is only from Allah, who is the Giver. 'Bi-tahqīq' means actualizing the wish for acceptance. Finally, al-‘Aṭṭār provides a lengthy grammatical note on the construction 'hā ana' (lo! I). He discusses its irregularity because hā usually attaches to demonstratives, but when the predicate is a demonstrative (like 'hā anta dhā'), it is acceptable. He cites authorities like Ibn Mālik, Hishām, al-Zamakhsharī, and Abū Ḥayyān, showing that this usage, while rare, has precedents in Arabic. This grammatical excursus demonstrates the author's philological rigor.

Key Terms
ها أنا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-‘Aṭṭār, what justifies the use of 'hā' with a pronoun like 'hā ana'?
A) The pronoun is in the nominative case
B) The predicate is a demonstrative noun
C) It is always allowed
D) It is a poetic license only

Key Takeaway
The irregular usage of 'hā' with pronouns is justified when the predicate is a demonstrative, linking the interjection to its natural host.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Resolving the Apparent Contradiction in the Introduction
Commentator resolves apparent contradiction between starting 'in the intended subject' and mentioning preliminaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and resolve apparent contradictions in a text by distinguishing between primary and secondary intent.

Core Idea
The introduction is intended secondarily, not primarily, so there is no contradiction.

When authors say they begin 'in the intended subject' but then mention an introduction BEFORE the intended subject, a careful reader might see a contradiction. The commentator resolves this by showing that 'intended' can mean two different things: primarily (the main topics) and secondarily (the introduction). This refinement is a common tool in Islamic scholarly writing to reconcile apparently conflicting statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The author first says 'I begin in the intended subject' (seeming to include the introduction), then says authors mention something before the intended subject (implying the introduction is not intended). Spot this tension.
2
Distinguish two meanings of 'intended'
The commentator introduces 'maqsūd bi al-dhāt' (primarily intended) and 'maqsūd bi al-taba'' (secondarily intended). The first statement refers to the secondarily intended (introduction), the second to the primarily intended (main topics).
3
Apply the distinction to resolve
Once you see that the first 'in the intended subject' includes both primary and secondary, and the later 'before the intended subject' refers only to primary, the contradiction disappears. The introduction is intended but not as the main subject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهَا أَنَا أَشرعُ في المقصودِ بعون المَلِكِ المعبود ; فأقولُ : قد جَرَتْ عادة أصحاب التصانيف بأن يذكروا قبل الشروع في المقصودِ بعضاً من الكلام، ويُسمونه المقدمة. (قَوْلُهُ: فِي الْمَقْصُوْدِ أي من الكتاب كان مقصوداً بالذات كمباحث : التصوراتِ والتَّصديقاتِ، أو بالتَّبع كالمقدِّمة . (قَوْلُهُ : فَأَقُولُ) عطفٌ على أشرحُ (قَوْلُهُ : جَرَتْ عَادَةُ أَصْحَاب التَّصَانِيفِ ) أي : جروا على عادتهم واستمروا عليها... (قَوْلُهُ : بِأَنْ ... إلخ) مُتعلِّقٌ بِجَرَت، وقوله : قبل الشروع في المقصود؛ أي : بالذات، والمقدّمة ليسَتْ منه، بل مقصودةٌ تبعاً بخلافِ قولِهِ أَوَّلاً : وَهَا أَنا أَسْرِعُ في المقصودِ، فإنَّ المراد منه ما يشمل المقصود تبعاً ، وهو المقدِّمة، فَاندفعَ مَا يُقالُ : إِنَّ أوَّلَ الكلام يُفيدُ أنَّ المقدمةَ مِنَ المقصودِ ، وآخرُهُ يُفيدُ أَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ منه، وهذا تنافٍ .
And I begin in the intended subject with the help of the King, the Worshipped; so I say: The custom of authors has proceeded that they mention some speech before beginning the intended subject, and they call it the introduction. (His saying: 'in the intended subject' means from the book, what is intended primarily like the topics of concepts and assents, or secondarily like the introduction. His saying: 'so I say' is coordinate with 'I explain'. His saying: 'the custom of authors has proceeded' means they have continued upon their custom. His saying: 'by that... etc.' is attached to 'has proceeded', and his saying 'before beginning the intended subject' means primarily, and the introduction is not from that, but is intended secondarily, contrary to his first saying: 'and I begin in the intended subject', for the meaning there includes what is intended secondarily, which is the introduction. Thus is repelled what is said: that the first part of the speech indicates that the introduction is from the intended, and the last part indicates that it is not from it, and this is a contradiction.)
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hāshiya) on the opening of the Sharh's introduction. The commentator addresses an apparent contradiction: the author first says 'I begin in the intended subject' (which seems to include the introduction as part of the intended), but then states that authors customarily mention something before the intended subject (i.e., the introduction is not the intended subject). The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between 'intended primarily' (maqsūd bi al-dhāt) and 'intended secondarily' (maqsūd bi al-taba'). The introduction is intended secondarily, not primarily. Thus, the first statement 'in the intended subject' refers to what is intended absolutely (including secondary), while the latter 'before the intended subject' refers to what is intended primarily. This distinction removes the contradiction. The commentary also clarifies that 'so I say' is connected to 'I explain' earlier.

Key Terms
مَقْصُود بالذات
مَقْصُود بالتبع
المقدمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not part of the intended subject at all.
B) It is intended primarily, like the topics of concepts and assents.
C) It is intended secondarily, as a means to the primary subject.
D) It is a separate, unrelated part.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in scholarly texts can often be resolved by distinguishing between primary and secondary intent of the author.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Three Perceptions of a Science's Preface
Author defines the preface of a science as three perceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three perceptions that constitute the preface of any Islamic science and apply this framework to a given science.

Core Idea
A science's preface is not just words but three essential cognitions that ground inquiry.

Traditionally, Islamic scholars open their works with an introduction. But this is not merely a formality; it serves an epistemological function. The author defines this preface as consisting of three distinct perceptions: a definition (tasawwur), an affirmation of the subject (tasdiq), and an affirmation of the need for the science. Understanding this framework will help you see how any Islamic science—from tafsir to fiqh to kalam—is methodically grounded.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three perceptions
In the Arabic, find the list of three items that the author says constitute the muqaddima. Notice they are: 'تصوره بتعريفه', 'التصديق بأن موضوعه كذا', 'التصديق بأنه محتاج له في كذا'.
The first is a conceptualization (tasawwur) and the other two are assents (tasdiq).
2
Distinguish tasawwur from tasdiq
Tasawwur is a concept without judgment; here it is the definition of the science. Tasdiq is an assent to a proposition; here it applies to both the subject matter and the need for the science.
This distinction is foundational in Islamic logic: all knowledge is either tasawwur or tasdiq.
3
Apply to a real Islamic science
Take the science of Usul al-Fiqh. Construct its preface: define it as 'the methodology of deriving rulings from evidence', state its subject as 'the evidences of Sharia', and state its need as 'to ensure correct derivation'.
This exercise shows how the framework applies to any discipline.
4
Check completeness
Does every Islamic science have these three elements? Consider 'ilm al-kalam: its definition is 'the science of divine attributes', subject is 'the existence of Allah', and need is 'to defend the faith'.
A complete preface should satisfy all three perceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأقولُ: قد جَرَتْ عادة أصحاب التصانيف بأن يذكروا قبل الشروع في المقصودِ بعضاً من الكلام، ويُسمونه مُقدَّمَةَ الشروع في العلم، كتعريف العلم، وبيان الحاجة إليه، وموضوعه. وتحصَّل أنَّ مقدَّمةَ العلمِ مجموع إدراكات ثلاثة: تصوره بتعريفه، والتصديق بأنَّ موضوعه كذا، والتصديق بأنَّهُ مُحتاج له في كذا. وتعريف هذا الفنّ آلة قانونية تعصمُ مُراعاتُها الذَّهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر.
So I say: The practice of authors has been to mention some speech before beginning the subject, and they name it the preface of beginning the science, such as the definition of the science, and the explanation of the need for it, and its subject. And it results that the preface of the science is a total of three perceptions: its conceptualization by its definition, the assent that its subject is such, and the assent that it is needed for such. And the definition of this art is: a legal instrument the observance of which safeguards the mind from error in thought.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage defines the introductory portion (مقدمة) of a science as standardly placed by authors before the main subject. It notes that this preface consists of three mental perceptions: (1) conceptualization (تصور) of the science through its definition, (2) assent (تصديق) that the subject matter is such-and-such, and (3) assent that the science is needed for some purpose. The passage then gives an example definition of the art of logic itself: 'a legal instrument that, when observed, safeguards the mind from error in thought.' This is presented as an instance of the first perception (definition). The explanation clarifies that the preface is not merely words but three distinct cognitions, addressing a potential misunderstanding that the preface is only verbal.

Key Terms
مقدمة
تصور
تصديق
آلة قانونية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three components of a science's preface?
A) Introduction, body, conclusion
B) Definition, subject, need
C) Tasawwur, tasdiq of subject, tasdiq of need
D) Terms, propositions, proofs

Key Takeaway
The preface of a science is a triple cognition: conceptualizing its definition, assenting to its subject, and assenting to its necessity.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
The Definition of Logic as a Legal Instrument
Author provides an example definition of logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to dissect the classical definition of logic using hadd analysis and test its completeness.

Core Idea
Logic is an instrument that safeguards the mind—its genus is instrument, its differentia is protection from error.

The passage not only describes the preface structure but also provides an actual definition of logic: 'a legal instrument the observance of which safeguards the mind from error in thought.' This is a textbook example of a complete definition (hadd). In this lesson, we will unpack this definition using definition analysis—identifying the genus and differentia and evaluating its inclusiveness and exclusiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The term being defined is 'this art' (هذا الفن) – i.e., the science of logic (mantiq). The definition is given immediately after describing the preface.
The definiendum is implicit but clear from context.
2
Extract the genus (jins)
The author places logic in the category of 'instrument' (آلة). This is its genus. Logic is a tool, not an end in itself.
Other instruments include language, but logic is a rational instrument.
3
Extract the differentia (fasl)
What distinguishes logic from other instruments? Its function: 'the observance of which safeguards the mind from error in thought.' The differentia is the protective role when properly applied.
This differentia is specific to logic; grammar safeguards language, not thought.
4
Test completeness of the definition
Does this definition include all instances of logic? Yes, all valid logic prevents error. Does it exclude non-instances? For example, mathematics also prevents error in calculation, but it deals with quantity, not thought as such. So the definition is precise.
A complete definition should cover all cases and exclude all others.
5
Evaluate the definition's strength
Consider if the adjective 'legal' (قانونية) is necessary. It emphasizes that logic is rule-based, like a canon. This strengthens the definition by highlighting its systematic nature.
Some later definitions omit 'legal' but the core idea remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأقولُ: قد جَرَتْ عادة أصحاب التصانيف بأن يذكروا قبل الشروع في المقصودِ بعضاً من الكلام، ويُسمونه مُقدَّمَةَ الشروع في العلم، كتعريف العلم، وبيان الحاجة إليه، وموضوعه. وتحصَّل أنَّ مقدَّمةَ العلمِ مجموع إدراكات ثلاثة: تصوره بتعريفه، والتصديق بأنَّ موضوعه كذا، والتصديق بأنَّهُ مُحتاج له في كذا. وتعريف هذا الفنّ آلة قانونية تعصمُ مُراعاتُها الذَّهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر.
So I say: The practice of authors has been to mention some speech before beginning the subject, and they name it the preface of beginning the science, such as the definition of the science, and the explanation of the need for it, and its subject. And it results that the preface of the science is a total of three perceptions: its conceptualization by its definition, the assent that its subject is such, and the assent that it is needed for such. And the definition of this art is: a legal instrument the observance of which safeguards the mind from error in thought.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage defines the introductory portion (مقدمة) of a science as standardly placed by authors before the main subject. It notes that this preface consists of three mental perceptions: (1) conceptualization (تصور) of the science through its definition, (2) assent (تصديق) that the subject matter is such-and-such, and (3) assent that the science is needed for some purpose. The passage then gives an example definition of the art of logic itself: 'a legal instrument that, when observed, safeguards the mind from error in thought.' This is presented as an instance of the first perception (definition). The explanation clarifies that the preface is not merely words but three distinct cognitions, addressing a potential misunderstanding that the preface is only verbal.
