Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Three Perceptions of the Introduction of a Science and the Distinction Between Muqaddimat al-'Ilm and Muqaddimat al-Kitab
Author explains the three perceptions constituting muqaddimat al-'ilm and distinguishes it from muqaddimat al-kitab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three perceptions that constitute the introduction of a science (muqaddimat al-'ilm) and distinguish it from the introduction of a book (muqaddimat al-kitab) using the criteria given in the text.

Core Idea
The introduction of a science is a set of three mental perceptions, not the verbal preface of a book.

In Islamic logic and the study of sciences, one must first understand what constitutes the introductory knowledge of a science. The commentators explain that this introduction is not merely the text at the start of a book, but a collection of specific conceptual and assertive perceptions. This lesson unpacks those perceptions and clarifies the distinction between the mental introduction of the science and the verbal introduction of a book.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three perceptions from the passage
Read the Arabic carefully to find where the author lists the three perceptions that make up muqaddimat al-'ilm. They are: a conception (tasawwur) of the science via its definition, and two assents (tasdiq) – one regarding its need and one regarding its subject matter.
The text states: 'مقدمة العلم مجموع إدراكات ثلاثة: تصوره بتعريفه، والتصديق بأن موضوعه كذا, والتصديق بأنه محتاج له في كذا.'
2
Understand the nature of each perception
The first perception is a simple conception (tasawwur), obtained through a descriptive definition (rasm). The second and third are assents (tasdiq), which are judgments: that the science is needed for a certain purpose, and that its subject matter is such-and-such. Note that the word 'clarification' (bayān) is used for the assents, not for the definition, because definition yields conception, not assent.
The commentator explains why the word 'clarification' was omitted from the definition: 'لأن ذكر التعريف إنما يفيد التصور'.
3
Distinguish muqaddimat al-'ilm from muqaddimat al-kitab
Muqaddimat al-'ilm is the sum of the three mental perceptions. Muqaddimat al-kitab is the verbal text placed before the main content. The passage shows that the two are distinct: the former is mental, the latter is verbal. Their significations have varying logical relations (generality, disparity, specificity in some respects).
The text explicitly says: 'مقدمة الكتاب ألفاظ، والثانية مجموع الإدراكات الثلاثة السابقة'.
4
Apply the distinction to a real Islamic science
Take the science of logic itself. Its muqaddimat al-'ilm consists of: a conception of logic as a legal instrument that safeguards the mind, an assent that it is needed to avoid error in thinking, and an assent that its subject matter is conceptual and assertive information. Now, find a book on logic and examine its verbal introduction: does it contain these three perceptions, or additional matters?
This step bridges the theoretical distinction to a practical Islamic science example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الشارح
مُقدَّمةَ الشروع في العِلم، كتعريف العِلم، وبيان الحاجة إليه، وموضوعه.
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: مُقَدِّمَةَ الشَّرُوع فِي الْعِلْمِ) أي: مُقدِّمةَ العِلْمِ المشروع فيه، وأضاف المقدِّمةَ لِلشُّروع ؛ لأنَّهُ يتوقَّفُ عليها بالمرَّة بالنسبة للتعريف وعلى جهة الكمال بالنسبة للباقي . (قَوْلُهُ : كَتَعْرِيْفِ ) أي : كَذكْرِ تعريف العِلْم المفيد، ذلك التعريف لتصورِ العِلْمِ الذي هو الإدراك الأوَّلُ، فَقولُهُ: كَتعريف تمثيل لذكْرِ البعض الذي جرت العادة بتقديمه على الشروع في المقصودِ، لَا أَنَّهُ مثال للبعضِ كَمَا لَا يَخفى، وتعريفُ هذا الفنّ آلة قانونية تعصمُ مُراعاتُها الذَّهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر على ما هو معلوم . (قَوْلُهُ: وَبَيَانِ الْحَاجَةِ ... إلخ) أي: وتبيين؛ أي: وذكر ما يفيدُ التَّصديق بأنَّ هذا العِلْمَ مُحتاج إليه في كذا كَعصمةِ الذَّهن عن الخطأ في الفكرِ، فإنَّهُ مُحتاج فيها إلى المنطق، فالتَّصديقُ بالعصمة المذكورة التي هي تابعةُ المنطق هو الإدراك الثَّاني ، إِنْ قُلْتَ: لِمَ أسقط لفظ بيان من التَّعريف وأضافَهُ لِمَا عداه؟! قُلْتُ : لَعَلَّهُ لما قالَهُ بعضُهم من أنَّ البيان شائع في ذكر ما يفيد التصديق، وذلك ظاهر في الموضوع والحاجة دونَ التَّعريف ؛ لأنَّ ذكْرَ التَّعريفِ إِنَّما يُفيدُ التَّصور . (قَوْلُهُ : وَمَوْضُوْعِهِ) أي: وتبيين؛ أي: ذكرُ مَا يُفيدُ التصديق بموضوعه، وهذا التصديقُ هو الإدراكُ الثَّالث، وموضوع هذا الفنّ المعلومات التَّصوريَّةُ والتَّصديقيَّةُ، فَقولُهُ: وَمَوضوعُهُ ؛ عطفٌ على الحاجة إليه ؛ أي وبيانُ موضوعه، إنْ قُلْتَ: المراد بالبيانِ التَّصديق، والشُّروعُ في العِلْم لا يتوقَّفُ على التَّصديقِ بِموضوعِهِ وَلَا على التصديقِ بالحاجة إليه، وإِنَّما يتوقَّفُ على التَّصديق بأنَّ مَوضوعَهُ كذا، وبأَنَّهُ يحتاج كذا، قُلْتُ : إليه في في كلام الشَّارحِ حذف مُضاف؛ أي : وبيان حاجيَّةِ الحاجة إليه في كذا، وبيان موضوعيَّةِ مَوضوعِهِ ؛ أي: بيان كونِهِ مُحتاجاً له في كذا، وبيانُ كَونِ موضوعِهِ كذا ، فَتحصَّلَ أنَّ مقدَّمةَ العِلْمِ مَجموع إدراكات ثلاثة: تصوره بتعريفه، والتصديق بأنَّ موضوعه كذا ، والتصديق بأنَّهُ مُحتاج له في كذا
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : كَتَعْرِيْفِ الْعِلْمِ أي : بِرسمِهِ، لَا بِحَدِّهِ؛ لاستدعائه معرفةً جميعِ مَسائلِ
الدسوقي
وأمَّا مقدِّمة الكتاب؛ فهي عبارةٌ عن ألفاظ قدمت أمام المقصود لارتباط له بها، وانتفاع بها فيه؛ سواء كانت تلك الألفاظ دالّة على متعلّق الإدراكات الثلاثة المعبَّر عنها بمقدّمةِ العِلْم فقط، أو على غيرها من المعاني فقط، أو عليها وعلى غيرها من المعاني، فَمدلولُ مُقدِّمة الكتابِ أعم(۱) مِن مُتعلّقٍ مُقدّمةِ العِلْم وظهرَ مِنْ هذا أنَّ مُقدِّمة الكتابِ مُباينةٌ لِمُقدِّمةِ العِلْم ؛ إذ الأولى ألفاظ، والثانية مَجموعُ الإدراكاتِ الثَّلاثةِ السَّابقة، وأنَّ النِّسبة بين مدلول مُقدِّمة الكتاب وبين دال مُتعلّق مُقدّمةِ العِلْم ؛ التَّبايُن، وأنَّ النِّسبة بينَ مُقدِّمة الكتاب ودالّ مُتعلّق مُقدّمة العِلْم ؛ العمومُ والخصوص من وجه فيجتمعان في ألفاظ دالة على المعاني قُدِّمَتْ أمام المقصود، وينفردُ مُقدِّمةُ الكتاب فى ألفاظ دالة على غير المعانى الثَّلاثةِ قُدِّمَتْ أمامَ المقصود، وينفرد دالُّ مُتعلّق مُقدّمةِ العِلْمِ في ألفاظ دالة على المعاني

،
العلمِ قبلَ الشُّروعِ فِيهِ، قالَ شارحُ سُلَّم العلومِ : مُقدِّمةُ الشُّروعِ لا يمكن أن تكون بحد العِلْمِ ؛ لأنَّ حقيقةَ العِلْم مَسائِلُه ، وهي أجزاء غيرُ محمولة، فلا يحدُّ بها، ولأنَّ حدّه موقوف على معرفة جميع تلك المسائل، فلو كانَ مُقدِّمةً؛ لزم توقُفُ الشُّروع في تلك المسائل على العِلْمِ بها، وهو دور ، ولأنَّه يلزم أن يكون المسائل خارجةٌ عَنِ العِلْمِ؛ لأنَّ المقدِّمةً خارجة عن ذلكَ العِلم .ا.هـ. واستفيد أنَّ المراد: الشروعُ على كمال بصيرة، فإنَّ أصل البصيرة لا يتوقَّفُ إلا على التَّصورِ بوجه ما ، والتصديقِ بِفائدة ما ، وأمَّا كمالُ البصيرة؛ فقد يحتاج فيه لزيادة، وذكرُ البيان في حيّز الحاجة والموضوع؛ للإشارة إلى أنَّ العِلْمَ المتعلّق بهما تَصدِيقي؛ أي: التصديقُ بغائيَّةِ الغاية وموضوعيَّةِ الموضوع، فإن قلت: كما صرَّحوا بكون الموضوعِ مِنَ المقدِّماتِ؛ فقد صرحوا بكونه جزءاً مِنَ العِلم، وبِكَونِهِ مِن مباديهِ التَّصورِيَّةِ ؛ فَمَا الفرق؟ فالجوابُ أَنَّ التَّصديق (۱) قوله أعم : أي مطلقاً وينافيه ما يأتي له في قوله : (وكذا النسبة بين مدلول مقدمة من أن العموم وجهي . .ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
إلخ)
Introduction of the commentator: Preliminaries of embarking upon the science, such as the definition of the science, and the clarification of the need for it, and its subject matter. al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'Preliminaries of embarking upon the science') means: the preliminaries of the science embarked upon. He added the article 'al-' to 'preliminaries' because the science depends on it absolutely with respect to definition, and in a perfective manner with respect to the rest. (His statement: 'such as the definition') means: such as mentioning the definition of the science that is beneficial, that definition for the conception of the science which is the first perception. So his saying 'such as definition' is an example of mentioning some of those things customarily presented before embarking upon the intended subject; it is not an example of 'some', as is clear. The definition of this art is: a logical instrument whose observance safeguards the mind from error in thinking, as is known. (His statement: 'and the clarification of the need... etc.') means: and clarification, i.e., mentioning what yields assent that this science is needed for such-and-such, like safeguarding the mind from error in thinking, for it is in need of logic for that. So the assent to the mentioned safeguard, which is subsidiary to logic, is the second perception. If you say: Why did he drop the word 'clarification' from the definition and add it to what follows? I say: Perhaps because some said that clarification is common in mentioning what yields assent, and that is apparent regarding the subject and need, but not the definition, because mentioning the definition only yields conception. (His statement: 'and its subject matter') means: and clarification, i.e., mentioning what yields assent to its subject matter. This assent is the third perception. The subject matter of this art is conceptual and assertive information. So his saying 'and its subject' is conjoined to 'the need for it', i.e., and clarification of its subject. If you say: The intended meaning of clarification is assent, and embarking upon the science does not depend on assent to its subject matter nor on assent to the need for it; rather, it depends on assent that its subject is such-and-such and that it is needed for such-and-such. I say: In the statement of the commentator there is an omitted genitive; i.e., clarification of the neediness of the need for it in such-and-such, and clarification of the subject-ness of its subject; i.e., clarification of its being needed for such-and-such, and clarification of its subject being such-and-such. So it follows that the introduction of the science is a sum of three perceptions: its conception by its definition, the assent that its subject is such-and-such, and the assent that it is needed for such-and-such. al-'Attar: (His statement: 'such as the definition of the science') means by its description, not by its definition, because that would require knowledge of all its issues? al-Dasuqi: As for the introduction of the book, it consists of words placed before the intended subject due to a connection to it and benefit from it in it, whether those words signify the referents of the three perceptions expressed by the introduction of the science only, or other meanings only, or both. So the signification of the introduction of the book is more general than the referent of the introduction of the science. From this it becomes clear that the introduction of the book is distinct from the introduction of the science, for the former is words, and the latter is the sum of the three preceding perceptions, and that the relation between the signification of the introduction of the book and the indicator of the referent of the introduction of the science is one of disparity, and that the relation between the introduction of the book and the indicator of the referent of the introduction of the science is one of general and specific in some respects. They coincide in words signifying the three meanings placed before the intended subject, and the introduction of the book is exclusive in words signifying other than the three meanings placed before the intended subject, and the indicator of the referent of the introduction of the science is exclusive in words signifying the three meanings? al-'Attar: the science before embarking upon it. The commentator on Sullam al-'Ulum said: The preliminary of embarking cannot be by a definition of the science because the reality of the science is its issues, which are incomposite parts, so it cannot be defined by them, and because its definition depends on knowing all those issues, so if it were a preliminary, it would entail the dependence of embarking upon those issues on knowing them, which is circular, and because it would necessitate that the issues be outside the science, since the preliminary is outside that science. End. From this it is understood that the intention is embarking with complete insight, for the basis of insight depends only on a certain conception and a certain assent to a benefit. As for complete insight, it may require more. The mention of 'clarification' in the context of need and subject indicates that the knowledge related to them is assertive, i.e., the assent to the purposefulness of the purpose and the subject-ness of the subject. If you say: Just as they declared the subject to be among the preliminaries, they also declared it to be part of the science and among its conceptual principles; what is the difference? The answer is that assent... (1) His statement 'more general' means absolutely, but this conflicts with what he later says: 'And similarly the relation between the signification of the introduction...' that it is general and specific in some respects. End. al-Sharnubi. Etc.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the classification of the introductory matters of a science. It begins by establishing that the introduction of a science (muqaddimat al-'ilm) consists of three cognitive perceptions: first, a conceptualization (tasawwur) of the science through its definition; second, an assent (tasdiq) that it is needed for a certain purpose; and third, an assent that its subject matter is such-and-such. The commentator, al-Dasuqi, explains that the definition of the science itself is mentioned only for conceptualization, not for assent, which is why the author did not use the word 'clarification' for it, reserving that term for the need and subject, which yield assent. A finer point is made: the initial dependence on these three perceptions is only for the basic insight necessary to embark on the science; for complete insight, more is needed. The passage then distinguishes muqaddimat al-'ilm from muqaddimat al-kitab (the introduction of the book). The latter is a verbal text placed before the main content, and it may include the three perceptions or other beneficial matters. The relation between the two is clarified: they are distinct in nature (mental perceptions vs. words), and their significations have varying logical relations (absolute generality, disparity, and generality-specificity in some respects). A quotation from the commentator on Sullam al-'Ulum argues that the introduction of a science cannot be a strict definition (hadd) because that would require prior knowledge of all the science's issues, leading to circularity. Instead, it is a descriptive definition (rasm). The passage concludes by responding to an objection about the subject being both a preliminary and a part of the science, explaining that it is preliminary in the sense of being required for understanding, not as a component.

Key Terms
مقدمة العلم
مقدمة الكتاب
تصور
تصديق
حد
رسم

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three perceptions that constitute the introduction of a science (muqaddimat al-'ilm)?
A) Conception of the definition, assent to its need, assent to its subject
B) Conception of the name, assent to its existence, assent to its usefulness
C) Verbal preface, table of contents, acknowledgments
D) Conception of the definition, assent to its author, assent to its validity

Key Takeaway
Muqaddimat al-'ilm is a mental construct of three perceptions (one conception, two assents), and it is distinct from muqaddimat al-kitab, which is a verbal text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the science of usul al-fiqh. Identify what would constitute its muqaddimat al-'ilm: what is its definition (conception), why is it needed (assent to need), and what is its subject matter (assent to subject)? Write a short paragraph.
?
Examine the first page of any Islamic logic textbook (e.g., the introductory text of al-Akhdari or Sullam al-'Ulum). Determine whether the verbal introduction (muqaddimat al-kitab) contains all three perceptions of muqaddimat al-'ilm, and if not, what additional content is present.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Distinguishing Book Introduction from Science Introduction
Commentator explains the classification of the author's preface as a book introduction vs. a science introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muqaddimat al-kitab and muqaddimat al-'ilm by analyzing the scope and content of an introduction in a classical logical text.

Core Idea
The book introduction is customary; the science introduction is the foundation of knowledge.

Al-Dasuqi's commentary on the author's preface clarifies a crucial methodological distinction: the prefatory material customarily presented before the main subject is a book introduction (muqaddimat al-kitab), not a science introduction (muqaddimat al-'ilm). The science introduction is the totality of the three cognitive acts (al-idrakat al-thalatha) that ground the entire discipline. Understanding this distinction helps you navigate classical texts and recognize the different roles of introductory material.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of introductions
Find the phrases muqaddimat al-kitab and muqaddimat al-'ilm in the passage. According to al-Dasuqi, the part customarily mentioned before the main subject is a book introduction, not a science introduction. The science introduction is the totality of the three perceptions.
Look for the commentary where he says 'this part... is a book introduction, not a science introduction'.
2
Analyze the author's phrasing
Al-Dasuqi criticizes the author's statement 'prefaced with it' because it implies the preface is a science introduction, whereas it is actually a book introduction. He suggests that saying 'prefaced with that part' would have been clearer. Understand why the distinction matters for the text's organization.
The author's wording could mislead readers into thinking the preface is part of the science proper.
3
Examine the role of the three perceptions
The science introduction is defined as the totality of the three perceptions (tasawwur, tasdiq, and qadaya). These foundational acts are what the science builds upon. This distinguishes it from the book introduction, which is merely customary.
Al-Dasuqi uses this to argue that the science introduction is not a specific part but the whole set of foundational cognitions.
4
Distinguish signifier vs signified
Al-Sharnubi's footnote explains that the introduction is a book introduction with respect to the signifier (the words) and a science introduction with respect to the signified (the meanings). This resolves the apparent contradiction: the same text serves two roles depending on perspective.
This is a deeper conceptual point: the medium vs the message.
5
Apply to a real text
Consider the preface of a classical work like al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya or al-Muwatta'. Is it a book introduction (customary) or a science introduction (foundational)? Use the criteria: does it discuss the three perceptions? Or is it just a customary greeting and purpose statement?
Practice makes this distinction operational.

فَمِنْ أجل ذلكَ صَدَّرَ المصَنِّفُ هذا المختصر بها، فقال بعد الفراغ مِنَ الخُطبة :
الدسوقي
الثَّلاثةِ ؛ أُخْرَتْ عن المقصود، وكذلك النسبة بين مدلول مُقدِّمة الكتاب وبين مُتعلّق مُقدِّمة العِلْم. وإذا عَلمْتَ هذا ؛ ظهر لكَ أنَّ هذا البعضَ الَّذي جَرَتِ العادةُ بِذكرِهِ قبل الشروع في المقصودِ؛ مُقدِّمةُ كتاب لَا مُقدِّمةُ عِلْمٍ، وأنَّ قولَهُ: وَيُسقُونَهُ؛ أي: وَيُسقُونَ متعلق مدلولهِ مُقدِّمة الشروع في العِلْمِ إذا كانَ مدلول ذلكَ البعضِ مُتعلِّقَ الإدراكات الثَّلاثةِ فقط، أو وَيَسقُونَ متعلّق بعض مدلوله؛ حيث كانَ مدلول ذلك البعض متعلّق الإدراكاتِ الثَّلاثة ،وغيره، فظهر لَكَ أنَّ مُقدِّمةَ العِلْم مَجموع الإدراكات الثلاثة؛ لا ذلكَ البعضُ وَلَا مُتعلِّقُ الإدراكات المذكورة، تأملْ
(قَوْلُهُ : فَمِنْ أَجْلِ ذَلِكَ) أي: الجريان .
(قَوْلُهُ : صَدَّرَ بِهَا) أي : بالمقدّمة المذكورة في قوله : ويُسقُونَهُ مُقدِّمة الشُّروع العِلْمِ، وقضيَّتُهُ : أنَّ المقدّمة المصدَّرَ بها هذا المتنُ؛ مُقدِّمةُ عِلْمٍ، مَعَ إِنَّهَا مُقَدِّمةُ كتاب كما هو ظاهرٌ مِمَّا سبق، فَلَوْ قَالَ : صدَّرَ بِهِ؛ أي بذلك البعضِ الَّذِي جَرَتِ العادةُ بتقديمه ؛ كانَ أَوْلَى . (۱) قوله: تأمل تأملناه فوجدناه خلاف المنصوص عليه من أنها مقدمة كتاب باعتبار الدال، ومقدم علم باعتبار المدلول، إذ الأولى ألفاظ والثانية معاني. ا.هـ. الشرنوبي.
The commentator's introduction: 'Because of that, the author prefaced this summary with it, and said after finishing the sermon: al-Dasuqi: the three; they were delayed from the intended purpose, and likewise the relation between the signification of the book's introduction and the subject matter of the science's introduction. And if you know this, it becomes clear to you that this part which is customarily mentioned before beginning the intended purpose is a book introduction, not a science introduction. And that his statement: 'and they give it to drink' means: and they give to drink the subject matter of its signification of the introduction to beginning the science if the signification of that part pertains only to the three perceptions, or they give to drink some of its signification since the signification of that part pertains to the three perceptions and others. So it becomes clear to you that the science introduction is the totality of the three perceptions, not that part nor the subject matter of the mentioned perceptions. Reflect. His statement: 'Because of that' means: the customary practice. His statement: 'He prefaced with it' means: with the introduction mentioned in his statement: 'and they give it to drink the introduction to beginning the science', and its implication is that the introduction with which this text is prefaced is a science introduction, although it is a book introduction as is apparent from what preceded. So if he had said: 'prefaced with it' meaning that part which is customarily presented, it would have been more appropriate. His statement: 'after finishing the sermon' – know that the author composed this book of his in logic and theology, so the scholars took the section containing logic and commented on it. Thus this text on which our commentator wrote is a part of the book that the author composed, not an independent text as might be imagined; this was informed to us by some of our teachers. al-'Attar: by the existence of the subject itself; it is part of the science, and its conception is among the principles, and affirmation of its subjectivity is among the premises. As for the conception of the concept of the subject, i.e., what is investigated in the science regarding its essential accidents, it has been explained in the science of logic. These are four matters relating to the subject. (1) His statement: 'Reflect' – we reflected and found it contrary to the stipulated text that it is a book introduction with respect to the signifier, and a science introduction with respect to the signified, since the former are words and the latter are meanings. End quote. al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) by al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar on the author's preface to a logical work. It addresses a methodological issue: the classification of the prefatory material as either an introduction to the book (muqaddimat al-kitab) or an introduction to the science (muqaddimat al-'ilm). The commentator begins by explaining the author's motivation: the author prefaced his summary with a certain introduction because of the customary practice (jaryan). Al-Dasuqi then clarifies that the part customarily mentioned before the main subject is actually a book introduction, not a science introduction. He supports this by analyzing the author's phrase 'and they give it to drink' (wa yusqunahu), interpreting it as referring to the subject matter of the introduction to the science, but only if that subject matter is limited to the three perceptions (tasawwur, tasdiq, etc.). If it includes more, then it is only a part of that. The science introduction, he concludes, is the totality of the three perceptions (al-idrakat al-thalatha), not a specific part. Al-Dasuqi then critiques the author's wording: if the author had said 'prefaced with it' (saddara bihi) referring to the customary part, it would have been clearer. Al-'Attar adds another dimension: the subject (mawdu') of a science is known through its existence (which is part of the science), its conception (tasawwur) among the principles (mabadi), and the affirmation (tasdiq) of its subjectivity among the premises (muqaddimat). Additionally, the conception of the concept of the subject is explained in logic itself. This distinguishes between the subject as a reality and the conceptual understanding. The footnote by al-Sharnubi notes a reflection: the introduction is a book introduction in terms of the signifier (alfaz) but a science introduction in terms of the signified (ma'ani). This passage is essential for understanding the structure of classical logical texts and the role of introductions.

مقدمة العلم

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Linguistic Status of 'Muqaddimah'
Commentators discuss the linguistic origin and function of 'muqaddimah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the linguistic process of naql (transfer) from wasfiyya (adjective) to ismiyya (noun) as applied to the term 'muqaddimah', and identify the two proposed paths of transfer according to al-Dasuqi.

Core Idea
The taa in 'muqaddimah' marks its nounhood as secondary to its adjectival origin, not feminine gender.

In this lesson, we examine the commentary on the very first word of the matn: 'muqaddimah'. Al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar do not simply define the term; they analyze its linguistic journey from an adjective to a noun. Understanding this transformation is crucial for appreciating how technical terms acquire their meanings in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base claim
The commentators state that 'muqaddimah' is originally an adjective (صفة). Find where al-Dasuqi says this in the Arabic.
The word was originally used to describe something that comes first.
2
Understand the two paths of transfer
Al-Dasuqi presents two possibilities: either the term was first applied to the advanced part of an army and then extended, or it was transferred directly from adjective to the name of the first of everything. Notice the role of idafa (construct phrase) in specifying the meaning.
The first path involves a medium (the army term), the second is direct.
3
Recognize the function of taa
Al-Dasuqi explains that the taa indicates the transfer (naql) from adjectivity to nounhood, serving as a sign that the nounhood is subordinate to the original adjectivity. Al-'Attar further clarifies that this taa is like the taa in 'allaamah' (very learned), which marks abundance.
The taa is not a feminine marker here; it is a derivational suffix.
4
Connect to the commentary chain
Al-'Attar refines al-Dasuqi's analysis by noting that some scholars disagree about the taa's function, but he supports the transfer interpretation by citing al-'Isam. Observe how the super-commentary adds nuance.
This shows the critical refinement (textual_operation_tag) of the original commentary.

الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : مُقَدِّمَةٌ)
هي في الأصل صفة، ثمَّ نُقِلَت للاسميَّة، فإما أن تُجعل اسماً لِلطَّائفة المتقدّمة من الجيش، ثمَّ انتقل منها على وجه الحقيقة أو المجازِ إلى أوَّلِ كُلِّ شيءٍ، ويتعيَّنُ المراد بالإضافة، فيُقالُ : مُقدِّمة الكتابِ، ومُقدِّمةُ العِلْمِ، وإمَّا أَنْ تنقل مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى اسم أوَّلِ كُلِّ شيءٍ، ويتعيَّنُ المراد بالإضافة، فعلى الأوَّلِ : النَّقل إلى مُقدِّمة الكتاب أو العِلْمِ ،بواسطة، وعلى الثَّاني : بِلا واسطة، وبهذا تعلمُ أنَّ التَّاءَ فيها لِلنَّقل مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ لِلاسميَّةِ، بمعنى أنَّ اللَّفظَ لَمَّا صار اسماً بغلبة الاستعمال بعدَ أنْ كانَ ،وصفاً وصارت اسميَّتُهُ فرعَ وصفيَّتِهِ؛ جُعِلَتِ النَّاءُ علامة على هذه الفرعيَّةِ، ثمَّ إِنَّ هذه المقدِّمة في تقسيم العِلْمِ إِلى التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، وَتَقسيمهما إلى البديهي والنَّظريّ، وتعريفِ النَّظر، وبيان الحاجة إلى المنطق، وتبيين موضوعه.
(قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ : هَذِهِ مُقَدِّمَةٌ) أشار بهذا إلى أنَّ لفظ (مُقدِّمة) مُعربٌ لَا مَوقوفٌ وَلَا مبني ؛ لعدم التركيب كما قيل .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : مُقَدِّمَةٌ) اختلفَ هَل تاؤها للنَّقلِ مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى الاسميَّة؟ لأنها في الأصل صِفَةٌ؛ ثمَّ نُقلت إلى مقدّمة الكتاب أو العلم، فأُلحِقَتِ النَّاءُ بها لهذا النقل، ومعنى كَونِ التَّاءِ للنَّقلِ مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى الاسميَّةِ ؛ أنَّ اللَّفظَ إذا صار بنفسِهِ اسماً لغلبة الاستعمال بعدما كانَ وَصفاً ؛ كانت اسميته فرعاً عن وصفيّتِهِ، فيُشبه بالمؤنَّثِ، فإِنَّ المؤنَّكَ فَرعُ المذكَّرِ، فتجعلُ التَّاءُ علامة للفرعيَّةِ ؛ كَمَا جعلت تا علامة للدَّلالةِ على كثرةِ العِلْم في قولهم : رجلٌ عَلامةٌ ، بناءً على أنَّ كَثرةَ الشَّيء فرع عن تحقق أصلِهِ، وقال بهذا جماعةٌ ؛ مِنهُم العصامُ فيما نُقِلَ عنه في حاشية منوطة بشرحِهِ على الوضعيّةِ، قالَ: إنَّ مقدِّمة الكتاب ومقدّمة الجيش؛ كلاهما منقول من
(Author's Introduction)
(An introduction); that is: this is an introduction, and it is with kasra of the dal.
Al-Dasuqi
(His statement: introduction)
It is originally an adjective, then it was transferred to nounhood. So either it is made a name for the advanced group of the army, then transferred from it, on the basis of literal or figurative meaning, to the first of everything, and the intended meaning is specified by the idafa, so it is said: introduction of the book, and introduction of the science. Or it is transferred from adjectivity to the name of the first of everything, and the intended meaning is specified by the idafa. On the first view: the transfer to introduction of the book or science is mediated; on the second: without mediation. And by this you know that the taa in it is for the transfer from adjectivity to nounhood, meaning that when the word became a noun by prevalence of usage after it had been an adjective, and its nounhood became secondary to its adjectivity, the taa was made a sign of this subordination. Then this introduction is about dividing knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, and dividing them into the intuitive and the discursive, and the definition of nazar, and explaining the need for logic, and clarifying its subject.
(His statement: i.e. this is an introduction) He indicated by this that the word 'muqaddima' is inflected, not a particle of our [؟] or indeclinable; due to lack of composition as was said.
Al-Attar
(His statement: introduction) There is disagreement whether its taa is for transfer from adjectivity to nounhood? Because it is originally an adjective; then it was transferred to introduction of the book or science, so the taa was attached to it for this transfer. And the meaning of the taa being for transfer from adjectivity to nounhood is that when the word itself becomes a noun by prevalence of usage after it had been an adjective, its nounhood is secondary to its adjectivity, so it resembles the feminine, for the feminine is subordinate to the masculine, so the taa is made a sign of subordination, just as the taa was made a sign for indicating abundance of knowledge in their saying: 'a very learned man', based on the fact that abundance of a thing is secondary to the realization of its origin. And a group holds this; among them al-Isam according to what was reported from him in a gloss attached to his commentary on al-Wad'iyya, he said: 'The introduction of the book and the introduction of the army; both are transferred from'
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a hashiya (super-commentary) on the introduction of the matn, where two commentators, al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar, analyze the linguistic status of the word 'muqaddimah' (introduction) and then outline the contents of the actual introduction. The lesson begins with al-Dasuqi's commentary: he explains that 'muqaddimah' is originally an adjective (صفة) and then was transferred (نقلت) to nounhood (اسمية). He presents two possible paths for this transfer: either it was first made a name for the advanced group of an army, then figuratively or literally extended to the beginning of anything (like the introduction of a book), or it was directly transferred from adjectivity to the name of the first of everything. In both cases, the specific meaning is determined by the idafa (genitive construction), e.g., 'muqaddimat al-kitab' (introduction of the book) or 'muqaddimat al-'ilm' (introduction to knowledge). He concludes that the taa (feminine marker) in 'muqaddimah' serves as a sign of this transfer from adjective to noun, indicating that the nounhood is secondary to the original adjectivity. He then briefly lists the contents of the introduction: division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, their subdivision into intuitive (badihi) and discursive (nazari), definition of nazar, and the need for logic and its subject. Next, al-'Attar refines the discussion: he notes a disagreement about whether the taa indeed indicates transfer from adjectivity to nounhood. He supports the view by analogy with the feminine taa, which indicates subordination (the feminine is subordinate to the masculine), and with the taa in 'allaamah' (very learned) which indicates abundance. He cites al-'Isam's gloss that both 'muqaddimat al-kitab' and 'muqaddimat al-jaysh' are transferred from their original adjective meaning. This passage guards against misunderstanding the taa as simply a feminine marker; it is a specialized linguistic device indicating derivation.

التاء
النقل من الوصفية إلى الاسمية

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Linguistic and Grammatical Analysis of 'Muqaddima'
Commentators analyze the linguistic and terminological nature of the word 'muqaddima' in the introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the grammatical transformation of the term 'muqaddima' from an adjective to a noun, and its significance in the context of introductory logical works.

Core Idea
The term 'muqaddima' is not just 'introduction' – it carries a history of grammatical transformation from 'vanguard' to 'preface'.

In the Islamic scholarly tradition, commentators often begin by dissecting the very first word of a text to clarify its meaning and scope. Here, the word 'muqaddima' is analyzed not merely as 'introduction', but as a term with a rich linguistic history. The commentators explore its origin as an adjective describing the advanced part of an army, its transfer to a noun, and the significance of the ta' suffix. Understanding this analysis helps you appreciate how precise terminology is established in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original meaning
The word 'muqaddima' was originally an adjective describing the advanced group of an army (the vanguard). Recognize this as the semantic root before any transfer.
2
Recognize the transfer to noun
The term was transferred from its adjectival meaning to a noun for the beginning of anything, including a book. Note the debate whether the transfer was direct or via the military term.
Al-Dasuqi mentions two possibilities: one mediated by the army vanguard, one direct.
3
Understand the role of the ta'
The ta' (تاء) suffix is not a feminine marker here, but a sign of transfer from adjectival to nominal status. It indicates that the noun-ness is secondary to the original adjectival meaning.
Compare to other uses like 'علامة' (very learned) where ta' marks abundance.
4
Analyze the grammatical properties
The commentators discuss whether 'muqaddima' is declinable (mu'rab) or not. They conclude it is declinable because it functions as a predicate or object in a sentence. This shows attention to i'rab even in terminology.
5
Connect to the logical content
This introduction covers the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, and the division into intuitive and theoretical. Understanding the term 'muqaddima' sets the stage for the entire science of logic.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ
(مُقَدِّمَةٌ)؛ أي: هذه مُقدِّمة، وهي بكَسرِ الدَّالِ، قال الدسوقي: (قَوْلُهُ : مُقَدِّمَةٌ) هي في الأصل صفة، ثمَّ نُقِلَت للاسميَّة، فإما أن تُجعل اسماً لِلطَّائفة المتقدّمة من الجيش، ثمَّ انتقل منها على وجه الحقيقة أو المجازِ إلى أوَّلِ كُلِّ شيءٍ، ويتعيَّنُ المراد بالإضافة، فيُقالُ : مُقدِّمة الكتابِ، ومُقدِّمةُ العِلْمِ، وإمَّا أَنْ تنقل مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى اسم أوَّلِ كُلِّ شيءٍ، ويتعيَّنُ المراد بالإضافة، فعلى الأوَّلِ : النَّقل إلى مُقدِّمة الكتاب أو العِلْمِ ،بواسطة، وعلى الثَّاني : بِلا واسطة، وبهذا تعلمُ أنَّ التَّاءَ فيها لِلنَّقل مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ لِلاسميَّةِ، بمعنى أنَّ اللَّفظَ لَمَّا صار اسماً بغلبة الاستعمال بعدَ أنْ كانَ وصفاً وصارت اسميَّتُهُ فرعَ وصفيَّتِهِ؛ جُعِلَتِ التَّاءُ علامة على هذه الفرعيَّةِ، ثمَّ إِنَّ هذه المقدِّمة في تقسيم العِلْمِ إِلى التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، وَتَقسيمهما إلى البديهي والنَّظريّ، وتعريفِ النَّظر، وبيان الحاجة إلى المنطق، وتبيين موضوعه. (قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ : هَذِهِ مُقَدِّمَةٌ) أشار بهذا إلى أنَّ لفظ (مُقدِّمة) مُعربٌ لَا مَوقوفٌ وَلَا مبني ؛ لعدم التركيب كما قيل. قال العطار: (قَوْلُهُ : مُقَدِّمَةٌ) اختلفَ هَل تاؤها للنَّقلِ مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى الاسميَّة؟ لأنها في الأصل صِفَةٌ؛ ثمَّ نُقلت إلى مقدّمة الكتاب أو العلم، فأُلحِقَتِ التَّاءُ بها لهذا النقل، ومعنى كَونِ التَّاءِ للنَّقلِ مِنَ الوصفيَّةِ إلى الاسميَّةِ ؛ أنَّ اللَّفظَ إذا صار بنفسِهِ اسماً لغلبة الاستعمال بعدما كانَ وَصفاً ؛ كانت اسميته فرعاً عن وصفيّتِهِ، فيُشبه بالمؤنَّثِ، فإِنَّ المؤنَّثَ فَرعُ المذكَّرِ، فتجعلُ التَّاءُ علامة للفرعيَّةِ ؛ كَمَا جعلت التاء علامة للدَّلالةِ على كثرةِ العِلْم في قولهم : رجلٌ عَلامةٌ ، بناءً على أنَّ كَثرةَ الشَّيء فرع عن تحقق أصلِهِ، وقال بهذا جماعةٌ ؛ مِنهُم العصامُ فيما نُقِلَ عنه في حاشية منوطة بشرحِهِ على الوضعيّةِ، قالَ: إنَّ مقدِّمة الكتاب ومقدّمة الجيش؛ كلاهما منقول من مأخوذة من «قدم» لازماً بمعنى تَقَدَّمَ»، كما يقال : مُقَدِّمَةُ الجيش للجماعة المتقدّمة منه . قال الدسوقي: وإِنَّما كانَ مُعرباً لوجودِ التّركيب تقديراً ، وإلى أنه خبر لمبتدأ محذوف، وهو غير متعين؛ لجواز نصبه بفعل محذوف ؛ أي: اقرأ مقدمة، وجزه بعامل محذوف ؛ مُقدِّمة . أي : انظر في (قَوْلُهُ : مَأْخُوْذَةٌ مِنْ قَدمَ) عبر بمأخوذة دونَ مُشتقة الذي هو أخص ؛ إذ الأخذ أعم من الاشتقاق ؛ ليوافق بحسب ظاهره مذهب البصريين : أنّ الاشتقاق من المصدر وهوَ الرَّاجح ، ولو عبَّرَ بِمُشتقة ؛ لوافق بحسب ظاهره مذهب الكوفيين دونَ البصريين، وإن كان يمكن تمشيتُهُ على مذهبهم بأنْ يُقالَ : مُشتق من مصدرٍ قدم. (قَوْلُهُ : لَازِمَاً) حالٌ مِن قدم، ولا يُقالُ : صاحب الحال لا يكونُ إلَّا اسماً ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : قدم قصد لفظه، والكلمة إذا قصد لفظها ؛ كانَتِ اسماً بنفسها، وقوله: (قدمَ لازماً)؛ احترزَ بِهِ مِن قدم المتعدّي ، وقوله : (بمعنى تقدَّم)؛ أي: وحينئذ فمعنى (مُقدِّمة) : مُتقدّمة ؛ أي : إنَّها مُتقدِّمةٌ بِنَفْسِهَا لا بجعل جاعل، ولم يُقيَّدُ (تقدَّمَ) بكونه (لازماً)؛ لأنَّه لا يكون إلا كذلك، ولا يرد زيدٌ تَقَدَّمَهُ عمرُو ؛ لأنَّهُ مِن بَابِ : الحذف والإيصال؛ أي: تقدَّمَ عليهِ؛ فَحذف الجار، واتَّصل الضمير بالفعل، وحذفُ الجار المعدّى للعامل لا يُخرجُهُ عَن كونه لازماً . (قَوْلُهُ : كَمَا يُقَالُ) هذا تنظير بكون مُقدِّمة هنا - بكسر الدَّالِ ـ بمعنى مُتقدّمة ؛ أي : كَالقولِ الَّذي قالُوه في مُقدِّمة الجيش، وقولُهُ: (للجماعة)؛ أي: الموضوعة للجماعةِ ؛ مُتعلّقٌ بِيُقالُ، وقوله: (منه)؛ الضمير للجيش. قال العطار: قدم بمعنى تقدَّمَ كما يفيده كلام صاحب المغرب؛ فإنَّهُ قالَ : قدم وتقدَّمَ بمعنى، ومنه مقدّمةُ الجيش ومقدّمة الكتابِ، وفي شَرحِ التَّلخيص مَا يُفيدُ أنَّ مقدِّمةَ الكِتَابِ ومقدمة العِلْمِ؛ منقولانِ مِن مقدِّمة الجيش أو مُستَعارانِ منها، ويؤيّدُهُ ما في الفائِقِ للزمخشري ؛ المقدَّمُ الجماعةُ الَّتي تتقدَّمُ على الجيشِ مِن قدم، بمعنى تقدم، وقد اسْتُعِيرَ لأَوَّلِ كُلِّ شيءٍ؛ فَقِيلَ : مقدمة الكتاب .ا.هـ. واختار آخرونَ أَنَّ التَّاءَ ليست
Introduction of the author. (An introduction); i.e., this is an introduction, and it is with a kasra on the dal. Al-Dasuqi said: (His statement: 'An introduction') It is originally an adjective, then it was transferred to nominality. Either it is made a name for the advanced group of the army, then transferred from it, in reality or metaphorically, to the beginning of everything, and the intended meaning is specified by the addition, so it is said: the introduction of the book, and the introduction of the science. Or it is transferred from the adjectival state to a name for the beginning of everything, and the intended meaning is specified by the addition. On the first: the transfer to the introduction of the book or science is indirect; on the second: without mediation. By this you know that the ta' in it is for the transfer from adjective to noun, meaning that when the word became a noun by predominant usage after it had been an adjective, and its noun-ness became secondary to its adjective-ness, the ta' was made a sign of this secondariness. Then this introduction is about the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, and their division into the self-evident and the theoretical, and the definition of nazar, and explaining the need for logic, and clarifying its subject matter. (His statement: i.e., this is an introduction) He indicated by this that the word 'muqaddima' is declinable, not uninflected or built, due to the absence of composition as was said. Al-‘Attar said: (His statement: 'An introduction') They differed over whether its ta' is for transfer from adjective to noun? Because it is originally an adjective, then transferred to the introduction of the book or science, so the ta' was attached to it for this transfer. The meaning of the ta' being for transfer from adjective to noun is that when the word itself becomes a noun by predominant usage after it had been an adjective, its noun-ness is secondary to its adjective-ness, so it resembles the feminine, for the feminine is secondary to the masculine, so the ta' is made a sign of secondariness, just as the ta' was made a sign for indicating abundance of knowledge in their saying: 'rajulun 'allāmatun' (a very learned man), based on the fact that abundance of a thing is secondary to the realization of its origin. A group held this, among them al-‘Isam as transmitted from him in a margin attached to his commentary on al-Wad‘iyya. He said: The introduction of the book and the introduction of the army; both are transferred from 'taken from 'qadima' as an intransitive verb meaning 'taqaddama' (to precede)', as is said: the vanguard of the army for the advanced group from it. Al-Dasuqi said: And it is declinable due to the existence of composition in estimation, and that it is a predicate of a deleted subject, which is not certain; because it is permissible to make it an object of a deleted verb, i.e., 'read the introduction', and to make it a genitive of a deleted operator: 'in the introduction'. That is: look at (His statement: 'taken from qadima') He expressed with 'taken' instead of 'derived' which is more specific, because 'taking' is more general than derivation, to superficially agree with the Basran school: that derivation is from the masdar, which is the preponderant view. If he had expressed with 'derived', it would superficially agree with the Kufan school without the Basrans, although it could be reconciled with their school by saying: derived from the masdar of 'qadima'. (His statement: 'Lāziman' (intransitive)) is a hal from 'qadima', and it is not said: the owner of the hal is only a noun, because we say: 'qadima' is intended as a word, and a word when intended as a word, it is itself a noun. His statement: 'qadima lāziman' is a caution against transitive 'qadima'. His statement: 'meaning taqaddama', i.e., then the meaning of 'muqaddima' is 'mutqaddima' (preceding), i.e., it is preceding by itself, not by a maker's making. He did not restrict 'taqaddama' to being intransitive, because it is only like that, and there is no counterexample like 'Zayd taqaddamahu 'Amr' because it is of the category of deletion and connection; i.e., 'taqaddama 'alayhi' (preceded him); so the preposition was deleted and the pronoun became attached to the verb, and deleting the preposition that makes the verb transitive does not take it out of being intransitive. (His statement: 'kamā yuqālu' (as is said)) This is a comparison that 'muqaddima' here - with kasra on the dal - means 'mutqaddima'; i.e., like the statement they made about the vanguard of the army. His statement: 'liljamā‘ah' (for the group); i.e., placed for the group; it is attached to 'yuqālu'. His statement: 'minhu' (from it); the pronoun refers to the army. Al-‘Attar said: 'qadima' means 'taqaddama' as indicated by the words of the author of al-Maghrib, for he said: 'qadima' and 'taqaddama' are synonymous, and from it is 'muqaddimat al-jaysh' and 'muqaddimat al-kitāb'. In the commentary on al-Talkhīs, there is what indicates that the introduction of the book and the introduction of the science are transferred from the vanguard of the army or borrowed from it. Supporting this is what is in al-Fā’iq by al-Zamakhshari: 'al-muqaddam' is the group that advances on the army from 'qadima' meaning 'taqaddama', and it has been borrowed for the beginning of everything, so it is said: 'muqaddimat al-kitāb'. End quote. Others chose that the ta' is not...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the commentary on the first word of the matn, 'muqaddima'. It is a front_matter section where the commentators (al-Dasuqi and al-‘Attar) explain the linguistic and grammatical nature of the term. They clarify that 'muqaddima' was originally an adjective describing the advanced part of an army, then through usage it became a noun for the beginning of anything, including the introduction of a book. The commentators discuss the role of the ta' suffix, arguing that it indicates a transfer from adjectival to nominal status, similar to the feminine marker. They also analyze the word's declension, derivation, and usage in logic. The passage highlights that this introduction covers fundamental logical topics: the division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent), the division into intuitive and theoretical, the definition of nazar (inquiry), the need for logic, and its subject matter. The commentators then delve into grammatical details, such as whether 'muqaddima' is declinable, the significance of the verb 'qadima' being intransitive, and the difference between 'taken' and 'derived' in relation to Basran and Kufan grammatical schools. The passage ends with a comparison to the vanguard of the army and references to other linguistic authorities.

Key Terms
مُقَدِّمَة (muqaddima): In this text, it refers to the introduction of the book (matn) and is analyzed as a noun transferred from an adjective originally meaning 'vanguard'. [Note: No significant shift; the term remains stable across Arabic works as 'introduction' or 'preface'.]
تاء النقل (tā’ al-naql): The ta' that indicates transfer from adjective to noun, marking secondariness of the noun-ness relative to the original adjectival status. [Note: This is a grammatical concept specific to Arabic morphology; not a term from logic itself.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentators, what was the original meaning of 'مقدمة' before it was used for the beginning of a book?
A) The first part of a speech
B) The vanguard of an army
C) A type of logical argument
D) A grammatical term for a derived noun

Key Takeaway
The term 'muqaddima' exemplifies how Arabic words undergo semantic and grammatical shifts, and commentators clarify such shifts to ensure precise understanding of logical terminology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Three Preliminaries for Commencing a Science
Dassuqi and al-Attar on the components of the introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three preliminaries (tasawwur by rasm, tasdiq of ghaya, tasdiq of mawdu'iyya) required to begin studying any Islamic science, and explain why the introductory definition of logic is by rasm, not hadd.

Core Idea
Before studying a science, you must conceptualize it, believe in its purpose, and accept its subject—this is the introduction's job.

Every Islamic science begins with an introduction that orients the student. The matn states that commencing a science's issues depends on three things, and the introduction contains the explanation of need and the definition of logic. Dassuqi and al-Attar unpack what these three things are, and al-Attar clarifies that the definition given is a description (rasm) because it uses the science's goal—a necessary concomitant—rather than essential properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three preliminaries
Find in Dassuqi's commentary where he lists the three things: tasawwur of the science by its rasm, tasdiq of its ghaya, and tasdiq of the subjectivity of its mawdu'. Note that the pronoun in 'what the commencement depends upon' refers to these three.
These three are standard for any science in the Islamic tradition.
2
Understand 'science' and 'issues'
Dassuqi explains that 'science' means universal rules (qawa'id kulliyya) and 'issues' (masa'il) are the propositions that constitute the science. They can be complete relations, universal or particular propositions. This sets the scope of the subject matter.
This matches how mutakallimūn and fuqahā' define their sciences.
3
Distinguish conceptualization from assent
The first preliminary is a conceptualization (tasawwur) of the science, but only to the level of a rasm (description). The second and third are assents (tasdiqat): that the science has a worthwhile goal and that its subject is indeed a proper subject for investigation.
Tasawwur here is not a full hadd; it's a preliminary picture.
4
Recognize the role of rasm in the introduction
Al-Attar states that 'explanation of the need' (bayān al-ḥāja) leads to a definition by rasm: the science is defined by its purpose (a lāzim). For example, logic is 'an instrument that safeguards the mind from error'—a description, not an essential definition.
The introduction aims to give a working idea, not a full ḥadd.
5
See how remote premises are handled
Al-Attar addresses an objection: if the premises of a proof are remote, they may be included. He replies that such premises are still part of the chain, so the three preliminaries remain sufficient.
This shows the commentators' concern for completeness.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن: ما يتوقَّفُ الشُّروعُ في مسائل العلم عليه، وهي مشتملة على بيان الحاجة إلى المنطق، وتعريفه.

الدسوقي: (قوله: في مسائل العلم) المراد بالعلم؛ القواعدُ الكُلِّيَّة، والمسائلُ إمَّا النِّسَبُ التَّامَّة؛ فتكونُ الإضافَةُ من إضافة المدلول للدَّالّ، وإمَّا القضايا الكلية المفصلة؛ فتكونُ الإضافةُ من إضافة الأجزاء لكلّها، وإمَّا القضايا الجزئية، فتكونُ الإضافةُ من إضافة الجزئيات لِكلِّيَّاتِها. (قوله: ما يتوقَّفُ الشُّرُوع في مسائل العلم عليه) الضمير راجع لـ «ما»، وذكر باعتبار لفظها؛ أي: أمورٌ ثلاثةٌ يتوقَّفُ ... إلخ، وهو تصوره برسمه، والتصديق بغايته والتَّصديق بموضوعيَّة موضوعه. (قوله: وهي) أي: المقدّمةُ مشتملة؛ أي: والمقدّمة هنا؛ أي: مدلولها، وهو الألفاظ المخصوصةُ الدَّالَّة على المعاني المخصوصة، والواو هنا للتَّعليل؛ أي: وإنَّما قُلنا: المراد بالمقدّمة هنا ما ذكر؛ لأنَّ المقدّمة هنا مُشتملةٌ ... إلخ. (قوله: على بيان الحاجة) أي: على مُتعلّق بيان ما يُفيدُ التصديق بالحاجة إلى المنطق، وقوله: (وتعريفه)؛ عطف على الحاجة؛ أي: وعلى مُتعلّق بيان تعريف

العطار: التّعريفُ غيرَ جَامع، والجوابُ أنَّ المقدِّماتِ البعيدة للدليل مُقدِّماتُ لدليل مقدِّمة الدَّليلِ، فَبِالنَّظرِ لِذلكَ؛ يتوقَّفُ عليها مُقدِّمةُ الدَّليلِ الثَّاني بلا واسطةٍ، فَلَمْ تَخرُجَ. (قوله: ما يتوقَّفُ الشُّرُوع في مسائل العلم عليه) أي: على العلمِ بِهِ، فلا يرد أن يُقالَ: إنَّ ما يتوقَّفُ عليهِ الشُّروعُ لا ينحصر فيما ذكر، فَمِنْهُ نَفْسُ قَدرَةِ الشَّخص وقُواه وملابسةُ الخبرِ بِقَصدِ تحصيل الكُلِّ، إلى غير ذلك. (قوله: بيان الحاجة) هو أنْ يبيّنَ أنَّ النَّاسَ في أيّ شيءٍ يحتاجون إلى المنطقِ، فذلك الشَّيءُ هو غايته، فيحصل بذلك معرفةُ العِلْمِ بِغايته، وهي تصوَّرُهُ بِرسمِهِ؛ لأنَّه يحصل منهُ أنَّه عِلْمٌ يفيد هذه الغاية، وهو مُلازِمٌ مُساءٍ له، والتَّعريفُ باللَّازِمِ رَسمٌ، فَعلمَ أَنَّ بيان الحاجةِ ينساقُ إلى خصوص التّعريف بالرسم لا بالحدّ. (قوله: وتعريفه) عطفه على بيان الحاجة)، وعطفه على الحاجة محوجٌ للتّكلُّف.
The matn's introduction: What the commencement of the issues of a science depends upon, and it includes the explanation of the need for logic and its definition.

Dassuqi: His saying: 'in the issues of a science' — what is meant by 'science' is the universal rules, and 'issues' are either complete relations, so the addition is of the signified to the signifier; or detailed universal propositions, so the addition is of parts to the whole; or particular propositions, so the addition is of particulars to their universals. His saying: 'what the commencement of the issues of a science depends upon' — the pronoun refers to 'what', and it is mentioned considering its word [as feminine]; i.e., three things upon which it depends ... etc.: its conceptualization by its description, the assent to its goal, and the assent to the subjectivity of its subject. His saying: 'and it' — i.e., the introduction includes; i.e., and the introduction here, i.e., its signified, which are the specific words indicating specific meanings, and the waw here is for explanation; i.e., and indeed we say: what is meant by the introduction here is what was mentioned because the introduction here includes ... etc. His saying: 'on the explanation of the need' — i.e., on the object of explanation that yields assent to the need for logic; and his saying: 'and its definition' — coordinated with 'need'; i.e., and on the object of explanation of its definition.

Al-Attar: The definition is not comprehensive, and the answer is that the remote premises of the proof are premises for the proof of the premise of the first proof, so with respect to that, the premise of the second proof depends on them without mediation, so they are not excluded. His saying: 'what the commencement of the issues of a science depends upon' — i.e., depends upon knowledge of it, so it cannot be objected that what commencement depends upon is not limited to what was mentioned, for among them are the person's own ability and powers and what pertains to knowledge with the intention of acquiring the whole, etc. His saying: 'explanation of the need' — it is that it is explained what people need logic for, and that is its goal, and thereby one obtains knowledge of the science by its goal, which is its conceptualization by its description; because from it one obtains that it is a science that yields this goal, and it is a necessary concomitant that is named after it, and definition by necessary concomitant is a description. So it is known that the explanation of need leads specifically to definition by description, not by definition. His saying: 'and its definition' — coordinating it with 'explanation of need', and coordinating it with 'need' requires straining.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation (sharh) of the matn that opens a logic text. Dassuqi begins by clarifying that 'science' means universal rules, and 'issues' are propositions of various types. The key phrase 'what the commencement depends upon' is unpacked as three things: (1) the conceptualization (tasawwur) of the science by its description (rasm), (2) assent (tasdiq) to its purpose (ghaya), and (3) assent to the fact that its subject is indeed the subject. The author then states that the introduction contains 'explanation of the need' and 'definition' of logic. Dassuqi explains that 'need' here means what yields assent to the need for logic, and 'definition' is co-extensive with that. Al-Attar adds a refinement: the earlier objection about 'remote premises' is answered by noting they become premises for a secondary proof without mediation. He also clarifies that 'what commencement depends upon' is limited to the three items; other factors like personal ability are not part of the science's introduction. Finally, he explains that 'explanation of the need' leads to definition by description (rasm) rather than by definition (hadd), because it identifies the science through its purpose (a necessary concomitant). This passage sets out the structure of the introductory material: it must give a rough idea of the subject, its benefit, and its subject matter.

Key Terms
الشروع
المسائل
بيان الحاجة
التعريف
الرسم

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Three Prerequisites for Commencing a Science
Author and commentator explain the three prerequisites for commencing a science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three prerequisites for commencing an Islamic science and distinguish between tasawwur and tasdiq in this context.

Core Idea
Before studying any science, you must conceive it, affirm its purpose, and affirm its subject.

Embarking on any Islamic science requires more than just picking up a book. The tradition teaches that three things must be in place: a clear conception (tasawwur) of what the science is, an acceptance (tasdiq) of its purpose, and an acceptance of its subject matter. This foundational structure ensures focused and fruitful study. The passage below, from the commentary on a classic logic text, unpacks these prerequisites and explains how they are embedded in the introduction of such works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prerequisites
Read the passage and list the three things on which commencing a science depends: conception (tasawwur) by description, affirmation of purpose (tasdiq bi-ghaya), and affirmation of subject suitability (tasdiq bi-mawdu'iyya).
The commentator explicitly states 'three things'.
2
Distinguish tasawwur from tasdiq
Tasawwur is a mental concept or definition, while tasdiq is an assent to a proposition. Here, tasawwur is a rasm (description) of the science, and tasdiq involves accepting propositions about its purpose and subject.
3
Understand the role of rasm
The definition of the science is a rasm, not a hadd. A rasm uses properties (like purpose) to describe the science, which is sufficient for beginning study. The passage shows that even defining the science by its purpose is a valid rasm.
Attar explains that defining by purpose gives a necessary concomitant (lazim).
4
Apply to an Islamic science
Apply the three prerequisites to a science like fiqh. Tasawwur: 'knowledge of practical shari'a rulings from detailed evidence'. Tasdiq bi-ghaya: 'extracting rulings from evidence'. Tasdiq bi-mawdu'iyya: 'acts of the mukallaf and their rulings'.
This exercise solidifies the abstract concepts.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن

ما يتوقَّفُ الشُّروعُ في مسائل العلم عليه ، وهي مشتملة على بيان الحاجة إلى المنطق، وتعريفه،

الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : فِي مَسَائِلِ الْعِلْمِ المراد بالعِلْمِ ؛ القواعدُ الكُلِّيَّة، والمسائلُ إمَّا النِّسَبُ التَّامَّة ؛ فتكونُ الإضافَةُ مِن إضافة المدلول لِلدَّالّ، وإمَّا القضايا الكلية المفصلة؛ فتكونُ الإضافةُ مِن إضافةِ الأجزاء لكلّها، وإمَّا القضايا الجزئية، فتكونُ الإضافةُ مِن إضافة الجزئياتِ لِكلِّيَّاتِها . (قَوْلُهُ: مَا يَتَوَقَّفُ الشُّرُوعُ فِي مَسَائِلِ الْعِلْمِ عَلَيْهِ) الضمير راجع لـ «ما»، وذكر باعتبار لفظها ؛ أي: أمورٌ ثلاثةٌ يتوقَّفُ ... إلخ، وهو تصوره برسمه، والتصديق بغايته والتَّصديق بموضوعيَّة موضوعه.
(قَوْلُهُ: وَهِيَ) أي: المقدّمةُ مُشتملة؛ أي: والمقدّمة هنا ؛ أي: مدلولها، وهو الألفاظ المخصوصةُ الدَّالة على المعاني المخصوصة، والواو هنا للتَّعليل؛ أي:

العطار
التّعريفُ غيرَ جَامع ، والجوابُ أنَّ المقدِّماتِ البعيدة للدليل مُقدِّماتُ لدليل مقدِّمة الدَّليلِ ، فَبِالنَّظرِ لِذلكَ ؛ يتوقَّفُ عليها مُقدِّمةُ الدَّليلِ الثَّاني بلا واسطةٍ، فَلَمْ تَخرُجَ . (قَوْلُهُ : مَا يَتَوَقَّفُ الشُّرُوعُ فِي مَسَائِلِ الْعِلْم عَلَيْهِ) أي: على العِلْمِ بِهِ، فلا يرد أن يُقالَ: إنَّ ما يتوقَّفُ عليهِ الشُّروعُ لا ينحصر فيما ذكر، فَمِنْهُ نَفْسُ قَدرَةِ الشَّخص وقُواه وملابسةُ الخبرِ بِقَصدِ تحصيل الكُلِّ، إلى غير ذلك
(قَوْلُهُ : بَيَانِ الْحَاجَةِ) هو أنْ يبيّنَ أنَّ النَّاسَ في أيّ شيءٍ يحتاجون إلى المنطقِ، فذلك الشَّيءُ هو غايته، فيحصل بذلك معرفةُ العِلْمِ بِغايته، وهي تصورُهُ بِرسمِهِ؛ لأنَّه يحصلُ منهُ أنَّه عِلْمٌ يفيد هذه الغاية، وهو مُلازِمٌ مُساءٍ له ، والتَّعريفُ باللَّازِمِ رَسمٌ، فَعلمَ أَنَّ بيان الحاجةِ ينساقُ إلى خصوص التّعريف بالرسم لا بالحدّ . (قَوْلُهُ : وَتَعْرِيْفِهِ) عطفه على بيان الحاجة)، وعطفه على الحاجة محوجٌ للتّكلُّف .

الدسوقي
المنطقِ المفيدِ لِتَصوُّره ، وقوله : ( وموضوعه) عطف على الحاجة أيضاً، وعلى متعلّق بيان ما يفيدُ التَّصديق بموضوعيَّة موضوع المنطق، وبهذا ظهرَ لَكَ أنَّ الاشتمال مِنَ اشتمالِ الكُلِّ على أجزائِهِ، وأنَّ البيانَ مُستعمل فيما شاع فيه من ذكرٍ ما يفيد التصديق بالنسبة للحاجة والموضوع، وفي غيرِهِ مِن ذكرِ مَا يفيدُ التَّصوَّرَ بالنسبة للتعريف . (قَوْلُهُ : وَسَتَعْرِفُ . . . إِلَخ) أي : وهذه الأمورُ الثَّلاثةُ الَّتي اشتملت عليها المقدّمة يتوقَّفُ عليها الشروع في مسائلِ العِلْمِ ، وستعرفُ ... إلخ)، وحينئذ ؛ يكون المراد بالمقدمة هنا ما ذكره .
Introductory [line] of the author: 'What the commencement of the problems of a science depends on, and it includes the statement of the need for logic, its definition, and its subject.' Dassuqi: 'His statement: "in the problems of the science" – what is meant by 'science' is the universal rules, and the problems are either complete relations, so the addition is of the signified to the signifier, or detailed universal propositions, so the addition is of parts to the whole, or particular propositions, so the addition is of particulars to their universals. His statement: "What the commencement in the problems of the science depends on" – the pronoun refers to 'what', and it is mentioned considering its verbal form; i.e., three things on which it depends... etc., namely its conception by its description, and the affirmation of its purpose, and the affirmation of the suitability of its subject. His statement: "And it includes" – i.e., the introduction includes; i.e., the introduction here means its signification, and it is the specific words indicating specific meanings, and the waw here is for explanation; i.e., we only said that what is meant by the introduction here is what was mentioned because the introduction here includes... etc. His statement: "The statement of the need" – i.e., the object of the statement of what gives affirmation of the need for logic, and his statement: "and its definition" is coordinate with 'need'; i.e., and the object of the statement of the definition...' Attar: 'The definition is not comprehensive, and the answer is that the distant premises of the proof are premises of the proof of the premise of the proof, so with regard to that, the premise of the second proof depends on them without intermediary, so they are not excluded. His statement: "What the commencement in the problems of the science depends on" – i.e., on knowledge of it, so it is not objected that what the commencement depends on is not limited to what was mentioned, for among them is the very ability of the person and his strengths and the connection of experience with the intention of attaining the whole, etc. His statement: "The statement of the need" – it is that he makes clear that people in whatever thing they need logic, that thing is its purpose, so thereby knowledge of the science by its purpose is obtained, and that is its conception by its description; because from it it is obtained that it is a science that yields this purpose, and it is a necessary concomitant (lazim) and named accordingly, and definition by the necessary concomitant is a description (rasm). So it is known that the statement of the need leads specifically to definition by description, not by definition (hadd). His statement: "and its definition" coordinates with 'statement of the need', but coordinating it with 'need' requires effort.' Dassuqi: '...of logic beneficial for its conception, and his statement: "and its subject" is coordinate with 'need' as well, and with the object of the statement of what gives affirmation of the suitability of the subject of logic. And by this it became apparent to you that the inclusion is the inclusion of the whole for its parts, and that 'statement' is used in its common sense of mentioning what gives affirmation regarding the need and the subject, and in other than that of mentioning what gives conception regarding the definition. His statement: "And you will know..." etc. – i.e., these three things that the introduction includes are what the commencement in the problems of the science depends on, and you will know... etc., and then the intended meaning of the introduction here is what he mentioned.'
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's introductory line. It clarifies the meaning of the three prerequisites for beginning a science: 1) conception (tasawwur) of the science through a descriptive definition (rasm), 2) affirmation (tasdiq) of its purpose (ghaya), and 3) affirmation of the suitability of its subject (mawdu'iyya). The commentator Dassuqi first explains the term 'science' in the phrase 'problems of the science', interpreting it as universal rules, and the problems are the propositions (either complete relations or universal or particular propositions). Then he identifies the three things that the commencement depends on. He notes that the pronoun in 'upon it' refers to 'what', and it is considered in its verbal form. Then he explains 'and it includes' meaning the introduction includes the statement of need, definition, and subject. The Attar sub-commentator then discusses that the definition is not comprehensive (non-jami') and provides an answer. He also clarifies that 'what the commencement depends on' means knowledge of it, and lists other things like personal ability that also depend on it, but the text focuses on necessary knowledge. He explains that the statement of need leads to a descriptive definition because knowing the purpose gives a concomitant property. Thus, the introduction provides a rasm, not a hadd. Dassuqi concludes by explaining that 'and its subject' is coordinated with 'need', and that the inclusion is of the whole for its parts. The three things are the prerequisites, and they are all included in the introduction. For example, in the science of fiqh, one must have a conception of fiqh (e.g., 'knowledge of practical shari'a rulings'), affirm its purpose (extracting rulings from detailed evidence), and affirm its subject (acts of the mukallaf).

التَّصوُّر
التَّصديق
الرَّسم

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Why the Division of Knowledge is Placed First in the Introduction
Author answers why the division of knowledge into tasawwur/tasdiq is placed first in the introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is placed before the statement of need, definition, and subject in the introduction to a logic textbook.

Core Idea
The division of knowledge is the foundation for demonstrating the need for logic's two parts.

This passage addresses a crucial structural question: why does the typical Islamic logic textbook begin with a division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and affirmation (tasdiq) before even stating the need for logic? The author explains that the very demonstration of the need for logic depends on this division, establishing a logical order that governs the introduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the imagined criticism against placing the division first. The objection is that the introduction is meant for need, definition, and subject, not for division.
The objection is cited in the commentary as 'what is said'.
2
Trace the dependency chain
Understand how the statement of need depends on the division. The need for logic is shown by pointing out that error can occur in theoretical knowledge, but to demonstrate the need for both parts of logic (conception and affirmation), one must first divide knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq.
The dependency is: commencement depends on need, need depends on division.
3
Analyze the order
See why division precedes need, need precedes definition, and definition precedes subject. Since need depends on division, division must come first. Then need leads to definition, and definition precedes the subject discussion.
The commentator uses transitivity: if A depends on B and B on C, then A depends on C.
4
Address the counterobjection
Someone might say that need can be shown without this division, simply by distinguishing necessary and theoretical knowledge. The answer is that the intended need is specifically for the two aspects of logic, so the division into tasawwur and tasdiq is essential.
The division into necessary/theoretical does not highlight the two-fold purpose of logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قَوْلُهُ: وَلَمَّا كَانَ... إلخ) جواب عَمَّا يُقالُ : المقدمة معقودة لبيان الحاجة والتَّعريف والموضوع، فلأي شيءٍ ذكر فيها تقسيم العِلْمِ وقدَّمَهُ؟ . وحاصل الجواب : أنَّ بيان الحاجةِ الَّذي هو من جملة ما يتوفَّفُ عليه الشروع؛ يتوقَّفُ على التقسيم، فيكونُ الشُّروعُ مُتوقفاً عليه أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ المتوقفَ على المتوقفِ على شيءٍ؛ مُتوقِّفٌ على ذلكَ الشَّيء، فَلِذَا ذكرَهُ، وإنَّما قدَّمَهُ على تلك الأمور؛ لأنَّ بيان الحاجةِ مُتوقّفٌ عليه، وبيانُ الحاجة يؤدّي إلى التّعريف، وبيانُ التَّعريف مُقدَّم على الموضوعِ، فَلَزِمَ مِن ذلك تقديمُهُ على جميعِهَا ، فَلِذَا قدَّمَهُ عليها . فإنْ قُلْتَ: بيانُ الحاجة لا يتوقَّفُ على تقسيم العِلْمِ إِلى التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، بل يكفي أنْ يُقال: العِلْمُ إِمَّا ضروري أو نظري، والنظريُّ قد يقع فيه الخطأ، فاحتيج إلى قانون يعصم الفكر عن الخطأ فيه ؛ وهو المنطقُ ، والجواب : إنَّ المراد ببيانِ الحاجة؛ بيانها على وجه يشعر بالاحتياج إلى قِسْمي المنطق وهما : الموصل إلى التّصورِ، والموصل إلى التصديق، فاحتيج حينئذ إلى تقسيم العِلْمِ إلى تصورٍ وإلى
His statement: 'And since...' etc. – an answer to what is said: The introduction is devoted to the statement of the need, definition, and subject; so why is the division of knowledge mentioned in it and placed before them? The summary of the answer: That the statement of the need, which is part of what the commencement depends on, depends on the division; so the commencement depends on it as well; because that which depends on that which depends on something is itself dependent on that something. Therefore, he mentioned it. And he placed it before those matters because the statement of the need depends on it, and the statement of the need leads to the definition, and the statement of the definition precedes the subject. So it necessarily follows that it be placed before all of them. So he placed it before them. If you say: The statement of the need does not depend on dividing knowledge into conception and affirmation; rather, it suffices to say: knowledge is either necessary or theoretical, and theoretical may contain error, so a law is needed to safeguard thought from error, and that is logic. The answer: The intended meaning of the statement of the need is to make it clear in a way that indicates the need for the two parts of logic, namely: that which leads to conception and that which leads to affirmation. So then the division of knowledge into conception and affirmation becomes necessary.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage explains why the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is included and placed first in the introduction. The objection is: the introduction is meant for need, definition, and subject; why add division and put it first? The answer is that the statement of the need itself depends on the division, because to show the need for logic as having two parts (conception and affirmation) one must first divide knowledge into those two. Since the need depends on division, the commencement depends on division indirectly. Moreover, the order is logical: division enables explanation of need, need leads to definition, definition precedes subject. So division must be first. A further objection: need can be explained without the division, simply by distinguishing necessary from theoretical knowledge. The answer: the need intended is specifically for the two aspects of logic, so the division into tasawwur and tasdiq is essential. For example, in the science of usul al-fiqh, one shows the need for usul by noting that deducing rulings from the Quran and Hadith can err, so a measure is needed; but to highlight the two parts of logic (conception of rulings and affirmation of proofs), the division of knowledge becomes necessary.

Key Terms
التَّقْسِيم
الضَّرُورِي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the division of knowledge placed first in the introduction?
A) Because it is the most important part
B) Because the need for logic depends on it
C) Because it is a condition for defining logic
D) Because it is derived from the subject

Key Takeaway
The division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is placed first because the demonstration of the need for logic (and thus the entire justification for the science) depends upon it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Examine the table of contents of any classical logic text (e.g., al-Qazwini's 'Shamsiyya'). Identify whether the division of knowledge into tasawwur/tasdiq appears before or after the statement of need. Write a brief explanation of why your observation supports or challenges the reasoning in this lesson.
?
2. A colleague argues that a simpler division (e.g., knowledge into necessary and theoretical) would suffice to introduce logic. Using the counterobjection addressed in this lesson, demonstrate why the two-part division into tasawwur and tasdiq is essential for highlighting the purpose of logic.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Why the Division of Knowledge Comes First
Commentator explains why the division into tasawwur and tasdiq is included and presented before need, definition, subject.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is placed before the need, definition, and subject in a logic introduction.

Core Idea
The division into knowledge types grounds the need for both parts of logic.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a natural question: why does the introduction include a division of knowledge, and why is it placed first? The answer reveals a key methodological principle: the justification for studying logic itself depends on showing that knowledge has speculative aspects in both conception and assent. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how the structure of the introduction mirrors the dependence of its components.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector asks: why mention the division of knowledge (tasawwur/tasdiq) in an introduction dedicated to the need, definition, and subject of logic?
The objection implies the division is not obviously necessary for those three topics.
2
Trace the dependence chain
The commentator argues that the explanation of the need for logic depends on the division. Then, because the need leads to definition, and definition precedes subject, the division must come before all three.
This chain ensures the order: division → need → definition → subject.
3
Assess the need for the deeper division
The commentator refutes the idea that the simpler division (daruri/nazari) suffices. The deeper division into tasawwur/tasdiq is required to show that logic has two distinct functions: one for conception and one for assent.
Without this, one could claim all conceptions or all assents are necessary, eliminating the need for either part of logic.
4
Summarize the ordering rationale
Thus, the division is primary because it establishes the need for both parts of logic, and the need then motivates the definition and subject. This logical priority dictates the introduction's structure.
The commentator's answer is dialectical, proving the order is not arbitrary but reasoned.
